<<EM_WEEK_BEGIN>>
DATA WINDOW: 15 June 2026 to 19 June 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM resolved into a split regime: North Asia remained the shock-insulated positive pole, with Korea and Taiwan still dominated by AI / semiconductor external strength, while China, Brazil and South Africa confirmed softer domestic-demand signals and Turkey remained reserve-fragile. The largest growth signal was China’s demand break — retail contraction and FAI deterioration offset only by externally supported IP — while Brazil retail and South Africa retail added consumer-softening confirmation. Poland was the key exception inside EM Europe, with activity improving but quality-mixed and inflation/core persistence keeping the policy read hawkish.

Inflation and policy constraints stayed adverse, but the taxonomy became more important than the headline direction. India WPI, South Africa CPI and Turkey reserves still printed peak-shock energy / oil-importer stress, creating relief optionality if Hormuz normalization becomes physical and insurable. Poland and Brazil were less oil-reversible: Poland core inflation rose to match headline, while COPOM cut but hardened inflation language, leaving domestic/core/fiscal constraints intact even if oil falls.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: -
Supporting evidence:
China delivered the dominant negative growth impulse: retail sales turned negative y/y, FAI missed sharply and property investment remained deeply negative, with IP resilience tied to exports / high-tech / front-loading rather than domestic absorption. Brazil retail fell 1.5% m/m and missed expectations, South Africa retail slowed, and India labour softened. Offsets came from Korea and Taiwan’s AI / semiconductor external strength, Brazil IBC-Br stabilization, Turkey IP rebound and Poland IP beat, but the broad EM demand signal deteriorated.

Labor: -
Supporting evidence:
The labour evidence was limited but softer at the margin. India unemployment rose to 5.5% versus 5.2% prior and beat the Reuters poll, with LFPR and WPR both falling and rural unemployment driving the deterioration. China’s urban unemployment improved slightly to 5.1%, but this did not offset the broader domestic-demand deterioration in retail, investment and property. The period did not establish a broad EM labour break, but the incremental signal was weaker rather than supportive.

Inflation: -
Supporting evidence:
Inflation pressure deteriorated across several channels. India WPI accelerated to 9.68% y/y, driven by fuel / crude and broader producer-cost pass-through risk; South Africa headline CPI rose to 4.5% y/y on fuel; Poland core inflation rose to 3.1%, matching headline and extending a four-month upward grind; Brazil COPOM raised its 2026 inflation projection despite cutting Selic. The key split is reversibility: India / South Africa / Turkey stress is more oil-linked, while Poland and Brazil retain domestic/core/fiscal inflation constraints.

Financial Conditions: ~
Supporting evidence:
Financial conditions were mixed rather than uniformly tightening. Brazil’s 14.25% Selic still preserves high carry, and COPOM guidance limited disorderly dovish repricing, but the easing path remains conditional. Turkey reserve drawdown kept TRY fragility alive, although the print was backward-looking to the pre-MoU peak-stress window and lower oil creates relief optionality. North Asia external surpluses and AI inflows remain KRW/TWD supportive, while CNY stays policy-managed despite weaker domestic data.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
Policy space narrowed more than it broadened. RBI faces imported wholesale inflation pass-through risk; SARB headline optics worsened even though the underlying fuel concentration is less hawkish; Brazil cut but hardened inflation language and kept future easing data-dependent; Poland core inflation keeps the MPC hike-risk debate alive; Turkey reserve drawdown keeps intervention / hike-risk alive. Oil relief could soften the constraint for fuel-led oil importers, but not for sticky-core Poland or domestic/fiscal Brazil.

C. FULL RELEASE ARCHIVE

MONDAY 15 JUN 2026

South Korea — Export Growth Revised / Import Growth Revised (May)

Release Date: 15 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 02:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Export Growth Revised: 53,4% | Prior: 53,2%
Import Growth Revised: 20,7% | Prior: 20,8%

Professional Market Commentary

The revised trade tape confirms the flash message rather than changing it: Korea’s export cycle remains dominated by the AI / memory-chip supercycle. The scout frames the release as a record semiconductor-led export surge, with export growth revised slightly higher and import growth revised slightly lower; the key caveat is concentration, not level weakness.

The professional read is supportive for Korea’s external balance, but not a broad-based domestic-demand story. The tape emphasizes record chip exports, strong shipments to China and the US, and a record surplus, while also flagging that non-chip breadth and Middle East trade disruption are masked by the semiconductor impulse.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a genuine external-strength confirmation, but the hierarchy is narrow.

Key signals:

exports were revised marginally higher from the flash
import growth was revised marginally lower
the core impulse is semiconductors / AI capex, not broad regional trade
the surplus is macro-supportive, but heavily concentrated
import acceleration partly reflects domestic resilience and higher energy/import costs
Middle East trade disruption remains masked by the chip boom

The key analytical distinction is between level and breadth. The level signal is clearly positive: record exports, record chip shipments, record surplus. The breadth signal is less clean: semis dominate, and the prior EM context had already warned that North Asia external strength is AI-cycle concentrated rather than broad EM reflation.

State transition: continuation — chip-led external strength confirmed, not broadened.

Context from prior regional live file: Korea had already been part of the positive North Asia external pole, with AI / semiconductor demand separating it from weaker domestic-demand EM stories. The latest trade revision reinforces that external-support theme, but does not remove the prior caveat that Korea’s growth signal is concentrated and vulnerable to chip-cycle rollover.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

KRW / Korea rates read is supportive but not cleanly hawkish.

Reaction-function map:

positive for Korea external balances and equity-linked macro sentiment
helps keep BoK easing urgency lower if chip demand remains strong
not a broad domestic-demand signal
should not be traded as a generalized Korea reflation impulse
more KRW-supportive through external surplus than through rates repricing

The next verification test is whether June export orders / PMI export detail confirm durable chip demand without renewed inventory distortion. A memory-price rollover or weaker AI-capex signal would challenge the current continuation read.

India — WPI Inflation YY (May)

Release Date: 15 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 08:30
Importance: ****

Reuters Data

WPI Inflation YY: 9,68% | Prior: 8,30% | Revised: 8,26% | Reuters Poll: 9,05% | Surprise: 0,630%

Professional Market Commentary

The professional tape is clear: India WPI is the most direct EM data manifestation of the energy shock in this session. The scout identifies fuel and crude as the dominant drivers, with the new WPI methodology / base-year transition complicating comparability and poll interpretation.

The important nuance is that this is not “only rebasing.” The wholesale cost shock is real, but the size of the surprise should be treated cautiously because the release coincides with a new series structure and a transition toward PPI-style producer-cost tracking.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a real cost-push shock, but the precise surprise magnitude is contaminated.

Key signals:

headline WPI accelerated sharply to 9.68% y/y
the beat versus Reuters poll is large
fuel / power is the dominant driver
crude / petroleum shock is the clean transmission channel
food inflation also rose, making pass-through risk broader than fuel alone
the new base-year / basket structure weakens clean comparability with prior WPI history
the new PPI transition means producer-cost information is becoming richer but harder to map mechanically into historical WPI reaction functions

The hierarchy is fuel shock first, pass-through risk second, methodology caveat third. This should not be dismissed as “only rebasing”: the fuel impulse is genuine. But the poll miss should not be over-read because forecasters may have been estimating against a partly obsolete series structure.

State transition: escalation — conditional; wholesale cost pressure has intensified materially, but the signal is partially confounded by rebasing and vulnerable to reversal if oil falls.

Context from prior regional live file: India had previously sat in the stronger EM bucket because growth momentum was robust while inflation was comparatively benign. This WPI print challenges that clean configuration through imported energy costs, but does not yet overturn the India macro regime because CPI and domestic demand remain less stressed than wholesale fuel inflation.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

INR / RBI implication is hawkish-by-circumstance, not a clean domestic overheating signal.

Reaction-function map:

RBI cannot ignore a 9.68% WPI print if it passes through into CPI / expectations
the immediate policy signal is monitoring / delayed pass-through risk, not automatic tightening
INR is exposed as an oil-importer FX leg if the shock persists
if the Hormuz / oil shock fades, India becomes a leading candidate for wholesale disinflation relief
the useful trade is conditional on energy confirmation, not on WPI alone

The next verification tests are fuel CPI, food pass-through, core goods pricing and June/July WPI under the new series. A quick fuel rollover would turn this from an inflation-regime break into a peak-shock print.

Turkey — Industrial Production Unadj MM (Apr)

Release Date: 15 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 09:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Industrial Production Unadj MM: 7,5% | Prior: 4,4%

Professional Market Commentary

Public coverage framed the release as a strong manufacturing-led rebound, with the scout noting that official commentary emphasized resilience and the strongest industrial rise in eight months. The same tape also flags a material quality risk: public commentary treats the print as clean strength, while the macro context argues for front-loading discipline because Turkey is an energy importer facing input-cost and logistics uncertainty.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is an activity improvement, but quality is not yet validated.

Key signals:

Reuters unadjusted m/m print is strong at 7.5%
official adjusted framing points to strong y/y and m/m production growth
manufacturing is the main driver
mining remains weak
utilities are softer on the monthly detail
public commentary is uniformly constructive
no independent professional pushback surfaced in the accessible tape

The hierarchy is manufacturing rebound first, front-loading risk second, Turkey macro-stability context third. The print matters because it partially offsets prior activity deterioration, but it does not neutralize the Turkey regime problem: reserves, inflation credibility and political / FX risk still dominate the macro map.

State transition: improvement — conditional, front-loading-suspect.

Context from prior regional live file: Turkey had already shifted toward a fragile stabilization watch after weak GDP, volatile reserves, high inflation and a near-50 PMI bounce. This IP print strengthens the activity side of that stabilization attempt, but remains vulnerable to reversal because earlier PMI detail already carried stockpiling and input-cost contamination.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

TRY read is marginally supportive but second-order versus reserves / CPI.

Reaction-function map:

stronger IP reduces immediate hard-landing risk
it does not relax the TCMB constraint if inflation / reserves remain stressed
it may be politically useful for the stabilization narrative
it is not enough to make high carry “clean” if reserve defense resumes
front-loading risk means the next activity prints matter more than the April level

The next verification test is June PMI / orders / inventories and the next reserve release. A give-back in production or renewed reserve drain would turn this into a false stabilization print.

Poland — CPI Final MM / YY (May)

Release Date: 15 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 09:30
Importance: **

Reuters Data

CPI Final MM: -0,30% | Prior: -0,30%
CPI Final YY: 3,10% | Prior: 3,10%

Professional Market Commentary

The final CPI print confirmed the flash estimate exactly: headline inflation at 3.1% y/y and -0.3% m/m. Statistics Poland reported May CPI at 3.1% y/y, with goods prices up 2.1% and services up 5.7%, while consumer prices fell 0.3% m/m. ([Główny Urząd Statystyczny][1])

The composition is not a clean fuel-only story. Food and goods helped headline disinflation, clothing and furnishings remained in deflation, but services and utilities stayed firm. Trading Economics’ GUS-based breakdown shows food/non-alcoholic beverages easing to 0.5%, housing/utilities at 5.0%, health at 5.1%, transport at 5.6%, recreation/sport/culture at 5.6%, restaurants/hotels at 4.5%, education at 6.0%, and fuel/lubricants for private transport up 12.3%. ([Trading Economics][2])

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a no-surprise final confirmation, with the live signal sitting beneath the headline.

Key signals:

final CPI confirmed flash exactly
headline eased marginally versus April
monthly CPI fell for the first time in a year
food/goods disinflation helped the headline
fuel and electricity still carry the Middle East / energy fingerprint
services inflation remains materially firmer than goods inflation
the final print does not resolve the underlying inflation question

The hierarchy is final confirmation first, headline easing second, services persistence third. The print is cosmetically dovish because headline inflation is easing and in line with flash, but the composition shows that Poland is not the same as South Africa or India: part of inflation is fuel-reversible, but the services component is domestic and more persistent.

State transition: no material change — final confirms flash; headline easing masks stickier underlying services pressure.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland had already been an EM Europe case where growth resilience and inflation persistence limited dovish policy space. The final CPI print does not change that trajectory: headline relief is real, but the services-heavy composition keeps the policy debate focused on underlying pressure rather than headline alone.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

PLN / MPC read is mildly dovish on headline, but not enough to neutralize hike risk.

Reaction-function map:

final CPI removes upside headline surprise risk
food/goods disinflation gives the MPC some optical comfort
services and utility pressure keep the hawkish debate alive
oil relief would help the fuel leg but not the services leg
the core print is therefore the more important policy input

The next verification test is whether services/core inflation rolls over. If it does not, headline energy relief will not be sufficient to turn the MPC dovish.

India — Unemployment Rate (May)

Release Date: 15 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 12:30
Importance: **

Reuters Data

Unemployment Rate: 5,50% | Prior: 5,20% | Reuters Poll: 5,30% | Surprise: 0,200%

Professional Market Commentary

The scout frames the PLFS labour release as genuinely mixed: headline unemployment rose, participation and work participation softened, rural unemployment drove the deterioration, but urban unemployment improved and the y/y comparison is less negative.

The dominant professional read is therefore not a clean labour-market break. The release is relevant for domestic demand, but it is secondary versus the WPI energy shock in the current India policy stack.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is mild deterioration, not a clean labour-regime break.

Key signals:

unemployment rose 0.3pp m/m and beat the poll by 0.2pp
LFPR fell, so labour supply softened
WPR fell more than LFPR, so employment contraction is not purely mechanical
rural unemployment drove the deterioration
urban unemployment improved
y/y comparison is less negative, with urban UR lower than May 2025
seasonality matters around the post-Rabi period

The hierarchy is rural deterioration first, participation/employment decline second, urban offset third. The release is relevant for domestic demand, but it is secondary versus WPI in the current India macro stack because the active policy constraint is imported cost pressure, not labour overheating.

State transition: deterioration — mild, partly seasonal.

Context from prior regional live file: India had previously been treated as a high-quality EM growth pole, with domestic demand and policy credibility stronger than most peers. The May labour print adds a softness caveat, but it does not by itself overturn the India resilience story because the deterioration is seasonal, rural-led and partly offset by better urban unemployment.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

INR / RBI read is limited.

Reaction-function map:

labour softening slightly offsets the WPI hawkish impulse
RBI focus remains inflation pass-through rather than unemployment alone
domestic-demand confidence should be watched if labour softness persists into June/July
the print is not enough to price a growth-policy pivot
relative to WPI, labour is a second-order release this week

The next verification test is whether June reverses the seasonal labour weakness. If unemployment keeps rising while LFPR remains under pressure, India’s growth-quality premium would need to be marked down.

TUESDAY 16 JUN 2026

China — Urban Investment / Industrial Output / Retail Sales / Urban Unemployment (May)

Release Date: 16 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 04:00
Importance: ****

Reuters Data

Urban Investment (YTD) YY: -4,1% | Prior: -1,6% | Reuters Poll: -2,0% | Surprise: -2,10%
Industrial Output YY: 4,5% | Prior: 4,1% | Reuters Poll: 4,3% | Surprise: 0,20%
Retail Sales YY: -0,6% | Prior: 0,2% | Reuters Poll: 0,0% | Surprise: -0,60%
Unemp Rate Urban Area: 5,1% | Prior: 5,2%

Professional Market Commentary

The China tape is now the central EM demand-deterioration block. The official / Reuters framing is that retail contracted, fixed investment missed sharply, property remained the main drag, and IP was the only offset. NBS reported May industrial value added up 4.5% y/y, retail sales of consumer goods down 0.6% y/y and 0.38% m/m, fixed-asset investment down 4.1% y/y in Jan-May, real-estate investment down 16.2%, and surveyed urban unemployment down to 5.1%.

The scout’s useful addition is signal hierarchy: China is not simply “weak.” It is supply-strong / demand-weak, with IP resilience likely tied to exports, high-tech and possible front-loading rather than domestic recovery.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a genuine domestic-demand break with an externally supported production offset.

Key signals:

retail sales missed and turned negative y/y
goods retail was weaker than catering / services
fixed-asset investment deteriorated sharply
property investment remains deeply negative
manufacturing investment also slipped, despite policy-supported / high-tech resilience
industrial output beat modestly
high-tech and equipment manufacturing remain the production bright spots
unemployment improved slightly, but does not offset demand weakness

The hierarchy is retail / FAI deterioration first, property drag second, IP offset third. This is not a balanced slowdown. It is a two-speed configuration: supply and external channels still work, but domestic absorption is failing to validate production strength.

The important macro distinction is domestic demand versus export-pull. If production is being sustained by exports / high-tech / front-loading while retail and investment deteriorate, the policy implication is not overheating but rising pressure for targeted demand support. The risk is that China exports weakness through goods surplus while importing less domestic reflation into EM commodity demand.

State transition: deterioration — domestic demand breaking; supply/exports remain the lone offset.

Context from prior regional live file: The prior EM archive already showed China’s external and credit optics offset by weak private-credit internals and CPI/PPI scissors. Today’s activity bundle confirms that pattern on the real-economy side: production and exports remain the support, but household demand, property and investment are the drag.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

CNY / China beta read is negative for domestic-demand confidence but not a simple hard-landing signal.

Reaction-function map:

raises pressure for July policy fine-tuning / stimulus delivery
weakens the China domestic-demand impulse into commodities and EM Asia
supports the “China Shock 2.0” risk if IP/export resilience persists while domestic demand absorbs less
CNY remains policy-managed; data weakness argues for support but also limits tolerance for disorderly depreciation
oil-importer relief from Hormuz normalization would help, but cannot replace domestic-demand stimulus

The next verification tests are July policy delivery, June retail rebound, property sales/investment, credit impulse and export order durability. A retail rebound plus targeted stimulus would soften the deterioration call; continued retail / FAI weakness would make the China block the dominant EM growth drag.

Brazil — Retail Sales MM / YY (Apr)

Release Date: 16 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Retail Sales MM: -1,5% | Prior: 0,5% | Revised: 0,7% | Reuters Poll: -0,6% | Surprise: -0,90%
Retail Sales YY: 1,00% | Prior: 4,00% | Reuters Poll: 1,95% | Surprise: -0,950%

Professional Market Commentary

The Brazil retail block strengthens the EM domestic-demand slowdown signal. IBGE reported retail trade sales volume down 1.5% m/m in April, y/y growth slowing to 1.0% from 4.0% in March, and the quarterly moving average flattening at 0.0% after +0.7% in the quarter to March.

The scout correctly frames the divergence: the bearish consumer-cooling read is real, but IBGE also points to a giveback after months of strong results and a record-setting Q1, so the print is not yet a standalone Brazil demand-regime break.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a meaningful consumption deterioration, with a high-base caveat.

Key signals:

headline retail fell more than expected
y/y growth decelerated sharply
the monthly decline was broad across categories
fuels and lubricants were the lead drag
extended retail also fell
the moving average flattened, rather than collapsing
Q1 high-base effects mechanically amplify the April disappointment

The hierarchy is consumer cooling first, rate-sensitivity second, high-base caveat third. The print lands exactly where Brazil’s reaction function is sensitive: consumption is slowing while policy is still restrictive and inflation credibility remains relevant.

This is not yet a clean recession signal. But it is clear evidence that the 14.5% Selic environment is transmitting into domestic demand, especially in discretionary and credit-sensitive segments. The fuel-led drag also keeps the release connected to the broader energy-shock tape.

State transition: deterioration — rate-constrained consumer cooling, with Q1 high-base caveat.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil had previously combined stronger services and still-problematic inflation, leaving the BCB constrained despite pockets of activity resilience. April retail weakens the demand side of that mix and increases the importance of the upcoming policy decision, but the high-base effect keeps the signal from becoming a full domestic-demand breakdown.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

BRL / rates read supports cautious easing, but not a free easing cycle.

Reaction-function map:

reinforces that restrictive rates are biting domestic demand
increases comfort for a small easing step if inflation credibility allows
does not remove the fiscal / expectations constraint
BRL carry remains supported by level of rates but vulnerable if easing is read as too dovish
the signal is more relevant for the local curve than for a directional BRL call alone

The next verification test is the COPOM decision and guidance, followed by May/June retail. A rebound would validate the Q1 high-base caveat; another contraction would confirm that consumer cooling is becoming persistent.

Poland — Net Inflation YY (May)

Release Date: 16 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Net Inflation YY: 3,10% | Prior: 3,00% | Reuters Poll: 3,00% | Surprise: 0,100%

Professional Market Commentary

NBP’s core inflation release shows the real Poland inflation signal: net/core inflation rose to 3.1% in May from 3.0%, beating the Reuters poll by 0.1pp. NBP’s core-inflation table shows May 2026 core readings including 3.1% for inflation net of food and energy, and the NBP release confirms the May core-inflation publication. ([nbp.pl][3])

The scout’s key point is the policy hierarchy: headline CPI eased, but core did not. Core is now matching headline at 3.1%, after a steady rise from 2.5% in February to 2.7% in March, 3.0% in April and 3.1% in May. That makes Poland the cleanest EM-Europe sticky-core case in this week’s tape.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is the live Poland inflation signal.

Key signals:

core inflation rose to 3.1%
the print beat consensus
core is now equal to headline CPI
the trajectory is a four-month upward grind
services are the likely carrier of persistence
this is not primarily an oil-reversible inflation impulse
the release supports the MPC hawkish / hike-risk debate

The hierarchy is core grind first, headline/core divergence second, policy implication third. Poland is different from India, South Africa and Turkey: in those cases, oil/Hormuz relief can plausibly reverse the dominant inflation or external-pressure channel. In Poland, oil relief helps fuel prices at the margin, but it does not directly solve services/wage/core pressure.

State transition: escalation — domestic core grind.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland had already been positioned as a stronger EM-Europe activity/inflation case, with less room for dovish repricing than fuel-led oil importers. The May core print strengthens that position by showing that underlying inflation is rising even as headline inflation eases.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

PLN / MPC read is hawkish and oil-independent at the margin.

Reaction-function map:

core inflation rising keeps the July hike debate alive
PLN gets support from the relative policy-risk angle
oil relief is not enough to fully neutralize Polish inflation risk
the MPC can look through lower fuel if services/core remain sticky
this release should sit closer to Brazil than South Africa in the EM inflation taxonomy

The next verification test is whether June core rolls over. If core stabilizes or falls, the May print becomes a late-cycle bump; if it rises again, hike risk becomes harder to fade.

WEDNESDAY 17 JUN 2026

South Africa — CPI MM / YY (May)

Release Date: 17 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 10:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

CPI MM: 0,7% | Prior: 1,1% | Reuters Poll: 0,8% | Surprise: -0,10%
CPI YY: 4,5% | Prior: 4,0% | Reuters Poll: 4,7% | Surprise: -0,20%

Professional Market Commentary

The South Africa CPI release is a headline inflation escalation with contained underlying detail. Stats SA reported CPI rising to 4.5% y/y in May from 4.0% in April, the highest rate since July 2024, with a 0.7% monthly increase; the official framing attributed the rise primarily to higher fuel prices.

The scout’s key contribution is the reaction-function distinction: this is structurally similar to India WPI in being energy-led, but South Africa’s underlying inflation is better behaved. The uploaded tape flags fuel as the dominant driver, ex-fuel inflation as flat, and the below-consensus print as dovish-leaning despite the higher headline.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a fuel-isolated inflation escalation, not a broad inflation regime break.

Key signals:

headline CPI rose to 4.5% y/y, the highest since July 2024
the monthly pace moderated versus April
the print missed the Reuters poll on both m/m and y/y
the scout attributes the entire impulse to fuel
food inflation eased
underlying / ex-fuel inflation remained contained
core inflation firmed but stayed materially below the headline shock

The hierarchy is fuel shock first, contained underlying second, SARB reaction-function relief third. This matters because the policy signal is different from Brazil: South Africa’s inflation problem is more exogenous and more reversible if the oil path normalizes.

State transition: escalation — fuel-isolated, at/near peak.

Context from prior regional live file: South Africa had already been running a fragile but not overheating macro configuration, with weak growth and inflation vulnerability driven more by shocks than domestic excess. This CPI print raises the headline constraint, but the contained ex-fuel signal keeps the regime from shifting into broad inflation pressure.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

ZAR / SARB read is less hawkish than the headline suggests.

Reaction-function map:

headline CPI is unhelpful for SARB optics
the downside surprise versus poll and fuel concentration reduce the hawkish policy content
if Hormuz normalization holds, South Africa is a cleaner disinflation beneficiary than Brazil
ZAR should read this more through oil and global risk than through domestic overheating
second-round effects remain the key falsification risk

The next verification test is petrol/diesel price normalization and June/July CPI composition. A fuel rollover with stable core would validate a peak-shock interpretation; broadening into core would invalidate the dovish-leaning read.

Brazil — Selic Interest Rate (17 Jun)

SIGNAL TENSION CHECK

Main contradiction: EM data are still printing the peak-shock regime just as the oil / Hormuz shock is beginning to reverse in market pricing, but the inflation taxonomy is now split between fuel-led / oil-reversible cases and sticky-core / domestic cases.

Why it matters: India, South Africa and Turkey have the largest disinflation / external-relief optionality if Hormuz normalization becomes physical and insurable; Poland and Brazil retain hawkish policy risk because domestic/core/fiscal inflation pressure is not fully oil-reversible.

Implication: Treat the MoU as a major inflection candidate, not a confirmed regime break. The correct EM trade split is no longer simply oil importers versus exporters; it is oil-reversible inflation/reserve stress versus domestic sticky-core policy constraint.

*** Turkey — Gross / Net FX Reserves (18 Jun)
Why it matters: Cleanest Turkey stress check. Reserves are still draining in pre-MoU data; the next weekly print becomes the key test of whether oil relief stabilizes TRY pressure.

RED TEAM QUESTIONS FOR JGM OR SECOND PASS SCOUT

DATA WINDOW: 9 Jun 2026 to 12 Jun 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM closed the window with a positive external / selective-growth impulse but a weaker policy-quality mix. North Asia delivered the strongest real-economy signal through China and Taiwan trade, Korea’s Q1 revision and Taiwan’s AI-capex import/export surge, while LatAm showed firmer Brazil services and Mexico industrial resilience. South Africa improved externally through current account and mining, but manufacturing confirmed a weak domestic industrial core; Turkey stabilized reserves and current-account optics, but only inside a restrictive, credibility-dependent policy regime.

The regime is therefore dispersion rather than broad reflation. China’s trade and TSF optics are offset by weak private-credit internals and PPI/CPI scissors; Brazil’s services rebound is overwhelmed for policy by above-tolerance IPCA; Mexico is the cleanest soft-landing candidate; Turkey remains in hawkish hold; South Africa is commodity/external-supported but industrially fragile. The week improves external buffers and selective activity, but deteriorates broad easing confidence.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: +
Supporting evidence:
China exports/imports and Taiwan trade delivered strong external / AI-linked growth signals; Korea GDP was revised higher; Brazil services rebounded 1.2% m/m; Mexico industrial output beat sharply; South Africa Q1 GDP beat modestly. The quality is uneven: China remains externally led, Taiwan is AI-cycle concentrated, South Africa’s manufacturing contracted, and Turkey’s external improvement is likely demand-compression-led.

Labor: ~
Supporting evidence:
The supplied archive contains no direct labor-market release. The activity mix does not imply a clean labor signal: Brazil services and Mexico IP support employment-sensitive domestic resilience, while South Africa manufacturing weakness and Turkey demand compression argue against a broad labor upgrade. The bucket remains unresolved rather than directionally positive.

Inflation: -
Supporting evidence:
Brazil IPCA accelerated to 4.72% y/y and moved above the 4.5% upper tolerance band; China PPI accelerated to 3.9% while CPI stayed soft, confirming cost-push without demand-pull; India CPI rose on food/fuel pass-through; Mexico PPI firmed despite softer CPI; Turkey remains inflation-constrained under a hawkish-hold CBRT. Food/crop supply relief and Brazil IGP-DI moderation are offsets, but not the binding policy signal.

Financial Conditions: +
Supporting evidence:
External buffers improved across several stress points: China’s trade surplus beat, Taiwan’s trade surplus strengthened, South Africa’s current-account surplus widened to 2.4% of GDP, Turkey gross/net reserves rose, and Turkey’s current-account deficit narrowed. The positive read is conditional because some improvement reflects import compression, gold/commodity windfalls or policy-pushed financing rather than broad private-demand strength.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
The week reduces broad easing confidence. Brazil IPCA locks the BCB into higher-for-longer; Turkey’s CBRT hold is hawkish rather than neutral; China still needs support because private credit is weak, but PPI cost-push narrows the policy box; India remains comfortable on level but faces food/fuel pass-through risk. Mexico is the main easing-compatible exception, with CPI back in band and IP rebounding.

The tape frames the customs release as a broad external-sector beat: exports accelerated, imports also strengthened, and the trade surplus beat consensus. Professional framing is constructive but not cleanly extrapolative: the export story is tied to high-tech, AI, semiconductors and autos, while the durability question is whether part of the May strength reflects front-loading, price effects or shipment timing rather than a persistent final-demand run-rate.

the wider surplus raises trade-politics relevance even if the macro signal is externally supportive

The primary signal is external resilience. The key caveat is that this is not yet proof of a sustained domestic-demand recovery: import growth helps, but the interpretation remains vulnerable to inventory, energy-cost hedging and pre-emptive shipment behaviour. Context from prior regional live file: The prior EM tape had already classified China as a two-speed economy, with services improving while manufacturing remained demand-fragile. The reaction-function read should stay restrained. This does not remove the need for policy support because the strongest signal is external / sectoral, not a broad household-demand recovery. It does, however, reduce immediate pressure for aggressive easing if paired with stable credit and no renewed property deterioration.

Rates / FX implication: supportive for the external-balance leg of CNY, but not enough to turn China into a clean pro-cyclical domestic-demand story. The next verification tests are June exports, AI / semis durability, trade-politics pushback, and the May credit release.

This is a qualified improvement in the inflation picture.

Key signals:

headline CPI printed below consensus
annual inflation returned inside Banxico’s target band
monthly CPI declined for the first time in two years

services inflation remains sticky and is the main quality problem

the fiscal / tariff channel means the oil shock is being absorbed rather than absent

The hierarchy is headline disinflation first, sticky services second, fiscally-cushioned energy third. The print validates the direction of Banxico easing more than it proves a structurally solved inflation regime. It lowers near-term headline pressure but leaves an underlying services / administered-price caveat.

State transition: improvement — qualified.

Context from prior regional live file: The prior EM tape was dominated by imported-cost and energy pass-through concerns rather than Mexico-specific inflation relief. This print pushes Mexico against that broader EM inflation trend by restoring headline CPI to the target band. The improvement is real at the headline level, but the broader EM cost-pressure regime still matters through services and producer-price risk.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release supports Banxico easing optionality, but should not be read as a green light for an aggressive easing cycle.

Policy implication: softer headline and lower core help justify the prior easing step and reduce near-term pressure to tighten. The limiting factor is core services and the risk that energy suppression is fiscal / administrative rather than market-driven.

Rates / FX implication: dovish at the margin for front-end rates, but not necessarily MXN-negative if real rates remain high and the disinflation path looks credible. The main risk is a later re-acceleration if energy caps, electricity tariffs or services pressures reverse.

Professional Market Commentary

The tape frames the NBS price release as a producer / consumer scissors: factory-gate inflation accelerated to a near four-year high, while consumer inflation remained soft. PPI reached 3.9% y/y, the highest since July 2022, while CPI stayed at 1.2%; the framing emphasized rising energy / raw-material costs, AI-linked demand in selected sectors, and limited ability for most manufacturers to pass higher input costs through to consumers.

Official NBS / Xinhua material confirms the split: CPI rose 1.2% y/y and fell 0.1% m/m, while PPI rose 3.9% y/y and 0.5% m/m, with the monthly PPI pace decelerating from April’s 1.7%. The market-relevant interpretation is therefore not broad China reflation. It is cost-push producer reflation against still-muted consumer demand.

The margin risk is downstream squeeze rather than demand-led pricing power.

State transition: deterioration — stagflationary mix.

Context from prior regional live file: China had already been described as supply-side resilient but demand-fragile, with weak final-demand transmission and a need for policy support. HF Take — Strategist Layer

This release complicates the China reaction function.

Policy implication: soft CPI and weak demand-pull argue for continued support, but rising producer prices reduce the cleanliness of an easing impulse if cost-push pressure threatens margins or leaks into consumer prices. The right interpretation is not hawkish PBoC risk; it is a narrower policy box where support is needed but broad reflation is not confirmed.

Rates / FX implication: CNY gets some support from the trade surplus, but the inflation mix is not cleanly bullish. Producer reflation without CPI pass-through can pressure downstream profitability and reinforce selective, targeted policy support rather than broad domestic-demand optimism.

Next verification test: May credit, June CPI/PPI, and whether PPI m/m keeps decelerating. A renewed PPI m/m acceleration plus firmer core CPI would move the read toward genuine reflation; sustained PPI m/m easing would confirm that the war / commodity impulse is peaking.

The release is TRY-supportive only at the margin.

Policy implication: a narrower deficit helps the credibility backdrop, but it does not create space for cuts while inflation and FX stability remain fragile. If the narrowing is import-compression-led, it also confirms the weak-demand leg that lets CBRT avoid a hike.

Rates / FX implication: supportive for TRY carry if paired with reserve rebuilding, but fragile if energy prices rise again or domestic demand recovers into import demand. The next verification tests are gross/net reserves, monthly trade energy bill, and whether current-account improvement persists without activity deterioration.

China — Total Social Financing / M2 Money Supply / New Yuan Loans / Outstanding Loan Growth (May)
Release Date: 12 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 11:02
Importance: ****

Reuters Data

Total Social Financing: 2 030,0B | Prior: 620,0B | Poll: 1 870,0B | Surprise: 160,00B
M2 Money Supply YY: 8,6% | Prior: 8,6% | Poll: 8,5% | Surprise: 0,10%
New Yuan Loans: 520,0B | Prior: -10,0B | Poll: 550,0B | Surprise: -30,00B
Outstanding Loan Growth: 5,5% | Prior: 5,6% | Poll: 5,5% | Surprise: 0,00%

Professional Market Commentary

The tape frames the PBoC credit release as a headline TSF beat with weak private-credit internals. China’s new yuan loans rose to CNY 520bn in May after April’s rare contraction, but missed the CNY 550bn forecast, with weak household and corporate demand still visible beneath the aggregate.

The scout’s key institutional point is composition: TSF beat because of bond / direct-financing support, while bank loan growth remains soft and outstanding loan growth hit a fresh record low. Authorities had used informal window guidance to major state banks after the April contraction, which makes the rebound less organic and more policy-pushed.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is the decisive confirmation that China’s domestic-demand problem remains unresolved.

Key signals:

TSF beat consensus by CNY 160bn
M2 was stable at 8.6% and slightly above poll
new yuan loans rebounded from April’s contraction but still missed consensus
outstanding loan growth slowed to 5.5%, matching poll but down from 5.6%
scout / Reuters framing indicates weak household and corporate loan demand
TSF composition is fiscal / bond-flattered rather than private-credit-led
window guidance means the authorities are pushing lending against weak organic demand
this confirms the CPI/PPI signal: producer prices are rising, but demand-pull is not strong

The hierarchy is private credit first, TSF headline second. The aggregate is not bad, but the demand-relevant internals are weak. China is not moving into a clean reflationary credit cycle; it is relying on government / direct-financing channels while bank credit to the private economy remains structurally soft. That is the cleanest confirmation so far that the trade beat was externally / sectorally strong, not a broad domestic-demand repair.

State transition: deterioration — private credit; continuation — weak demand.

Context from prior regional live file: China had already been classified as supply-side resilient but demand-fragile, with weak credit demand and soft final-demand transmission. The May credit release confirms that prior regime rather than resolving it: TSF can be supported by public financing, but bank-loan growth remains weak. China therefore remains in a policy-push / demand-deficiency configuration.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release reinforces the case for continued policy support, but not because growth is collapsing; because private-credit transmission is weak.

Policy implication: PBoC / fiscal support pressure stays live. Soft CPI and weak loan demand argue for support, while the PPI cost-push shock limits the comfort of broad reflation trades. The likely policy mix remains targeted credit / fiscal support rather than a clean private-sector credit upswing.

Rates / FX implication: CNH should not trade the TSF beat as a clean domestic reflation signal. The better framework is: external surplus supports the currency, but weak private credit and margin-squeeze risk cap domestic beta. The next verification test is whether household and corporate loans recover without window guidance and without reliance on government bond financing.

India — CPI Inflation YY (May)
Release Date: 12 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 12:30
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

CPI Inflation YY: 3,93% | Prior: 3,48% | Poll: 4,00% | Surprise: -0,070%

Professional Market Commentary

The tape frames India CPI as benign on level but less benign in direction. May retail inflation rose to 3.93% y/y from 3.48%, slightly below the 4.0% poll, with food inflation up to 4.78% from 4.20% and transport inflation affected by state-run fuel companies hiking prices four times in May.

The scout’s key point is the turning-point risk: the level remains near the RBI midpoint and below consensus, but food and fuel are the wrong composition for forward comfort. The first fuel-price increases in years are the leading edge of war-energy pass-through after a period of absorption.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a mild reflation print, not an RBI stress print yet.

Key signals:

CPI rose to 3.93% from 3.48%
the print undershot consensus by 0.07pp
inflation remains inside the RBI 4% ±2% tolerance band and close to the midpoint
food inflation accelerated in the scout / Reuters detail
rural inflation remains above urban inflation in the scout detail
fuel-price pass-through is now starting after state fuel hikes
the composition is less benign than the headline miss because food and fuel are the key forward-risk channels

The hierarchy is level comfort first, directional deterioration second, fuel / food pipeline risk third. India is not in a Brazil-style inflation constraint, but the release shows that the war-energy shock is beginning to move from suppressed cost to retail pass-through. The print therefore reduces confidence in a one-way benign inflation regime even though it does not yet constrain RBI aggressively.

State transition: continuation — mild reflation.

Context from prior regional live file: India had previously looked comparatively benign within EM because inflation was not the primary stress point versus Turkey or Brazil. This print preserves that relative comfort on level, but adds a forward-risk channel through food and fuel. India therefore remains RBI-comfortable, but no longer purely disinflationary.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release keeps RBI comfortable near term, but raises the monitoring bar.

Policy implication: a sub-poll 3.93% print does not force a hawkish response. The issue is whether fuel repricing and food volatility persist into June/July. If they do, India moves from benign inflation to late-cycle pass-through risk.

Rates / FX implication: neutral-to-mildly hawkish at the margin. INR sensitivity should be more about oil / external balance than this CPI level alone. The next verification test is whether fuel hikes continue and whether food inflation reverses after the tomato / vegetable impulse.

The tape frames IPCA as the binding Brazil inflation release of the week. May IPCA rose 0.58% m/m versus a 0.53% forecast and accelerated to 4.72% y/y, above the central bank’s 3% ±1.5pp target range, with the print arriving just ahead of the next policy decision.

This resolves the earlier Brazil ambiguity. IGP-DI decelerated and crop supply is food-disinflationary, but the policy-relevant consumer gauge is accelerating above the tolerance ceiling. This is the key Brazil deterioration block.

the trajectory is steadily deteriorating from the Q1 lows
Brazil services had already shown domestic-demand resilience
IGP-DI deceleration did not translate into consumer disinflation
food/grain supply relief is not enough to offset the binding fuel / services / demand inflation constraint

The hierarchy is policy gauge first, above-ceiling level second, services/demand interaction third. This is not a benign inflation print. The monthly pace eased mechanically, but the annual level, surprise direction and policy threshold matter more. Brazil’s macro configuration is now clearer: domestic activity is resilient, services are firm, and the official CPI target gauge is above tolerance. That makes the BCB constraint tighter, not looser.

State transition: deterioration — above-target acceleration.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil had already been a two-sided commodity story: external/BRL support from commodities, but inflation and private-sector cost pressure from the war shock. IPCA confirms the inflation side is binding despite IGP-DI moderation and crop-supply relief. Brazil therefore shifts from ambiguous pipeline relief to official-CPI constraint.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release locks Brazil into higher-for-longer.

Policy implication: BCB easing risk should be marked down unless the next prints show a fast reversal in fuel, services or expectations. This release is more important than IGP-DI for the reaction function because IPCA is the official target gauge.

Rates / FX implication: supportive for front-end rates and potentially BRL carry, but not risk-free if the inflation overshoot reflects adverse energy/fiscal shocks rather than healthy overheating. The next verification tests are IPCA services, fuel/transport pass-through, inflation expectations and whether food/grain disinflation begins to offset the energy shock.

Poland — Current Account (Apr)
Release Date: 12 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: **

Reuters Data

Current Account: -1 558M | Prior: -234M | Poll: -114M | Surprise: -1 444,0M

Professional Market Commentary

The tape frames the Poland current-account release as a large headline miss, but not automatically an external-stress event. NBP reported that April exports of goods reached PLN 118.1bn while imports reached PLN 126.6bn, creating a goods deficit of PLN 8.4bn; the primary-income deficit was PLN 12.5bn, while the services surplus was PLN 14.7bn.

Public market summaries show the current-account deficit at €1.558bn, the largest since December, with the goods gap widening because imports rose faster than exports. The scout’s read is import-led deterioration inside an otherwise still-healthy Poland macro frame. The unresolved question is whether the import impulse is investment/domestic-demand positive or energy-bill negative.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is an external deterioration, but likely not a classic balance-of-payments stress signal.

Key signals:

current-account deficit widened to -1.558B
the print missed consensus by -1.444B
the deficit was much wider than the prior -234M
goods deficit widened as imports outpaced exports
services surplus remains a structural cushion
primary-income deficit remains material
the macro interpretation depends on whether imports are investment / demand-led or energy-cost-led

The hierarchy is headline external miss first, robust services cushion second, import-composition ambiguity third. The release matters because it is a large downside surprise, but Poland is not Turkey. The policy context is lower inflation and an easing-biased NBP, so the current-account miss is a monitoring item unless it becomes persistent or energy-driven.

State transition: deterioration — external, likely benign.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland’s prior EM role was relatively low-stress versus Turkey and Brazil, with the main focus on growth/inflation balance rather than external fragility. The April current-account miss introduces an external-monitoring channel, but the services surplus and likely import-led growth story prevent a full regime downgrade. Poland remains an easing CEE outlier unless the import bill proves energy-driven and persistent.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release is PLN-negative at the margin but not enough to overturn the easing / domestic-growth frame.

Policy implication: NBP can still ease if inflation remains low, but a persistent energy-led current-account widening would complicate the external side of the easing story. The key is composition, not the headline deficit alone.

Rates / FX implication: watch PLN sensitivity to import-led deficits if oil remains elevated. If imports are investment goods, the signal is less negative; if energy costs dominate, it becomes a war-drag external channel. The next verification tests are import composition, energy bill, services surplus persistence and NBP inflation data.

SIGNAL TENSION CHECK

Main contradiction: EM is showing external, tech and selected domestic resilience, but the inflation / policy quality is deteriorating and the domestic transmission is uneven. China has strong trade and TSF optics, but CPI/PPI and loan internals show cost-push plus weak private demand; Brazil combines firm services with above-ceiling IPCA; Turkey has better reserves and a narrower current account but remains in hawkish hold; South Africa’s external/mining strength is offset by manufacturing contraction; Mexico is the cleaner soft-landing exception.
Why it matters: This is not broad reflation and not a clean easing cycle. It is a dispersion regime: external winners and reserve buffers coexist with inflation constraints, weak private-demand transmission and two-speed productive economies.
Implication: The week’s state transition is positive for external buffers and selective growth, but negative for broad easing confidence.

5 KEY RELEASES TO DIG INTO

**** China — Total Social Financing / M2 / New Yuan Loans / Outstanding Loan Growth (12 Jun)
Why it matters: Decisive confirmation that China’s TSF headline beat is not a clean private-credit recovery; weak loan internals validate the demand-deficiency read.

**** Brazil — IPCA Inflation (12 Jun)
Why it matters: Binding Brazil policy gauge; y/y above the 4.5% tolerance ceiling, resolving the earlier IGP-DI ambiguity against the easing case.

**** China — CPI / PPI (10 Jun)
Why it matters: Most important macro-quality warning in China: PPI acceleration with soft CPI shifts the story from external resilience toward producer-cost squeeze / weak demand-pull.

**** Turkey — CBT Rate Decision (11 Jun)
Why it matters: Fully expected hold, but reaction-function signal is hawkish: easing cycle remains suspended, tightening bias remains available, and TRY credibility depends on reserves / inflation.

**** Taiwan — Trade Balance / Exports / Imports (9 Jun)
Why it matters: Strongest quality growth signal; exports and imports both surged, suggesting AI-capex strength plus capacity build rather than a one-sided trade spike.

RED TEAM QUESTIONS FOR JGM OR SECOND PASS SCOUT

Does China credit prove policy is pushing on a string, or is the TSF composition enough to keep nominal activity supported?

Does Brazil IPCA now fully kill the BCB easing case, or can food/grain disinflation and a later fuel reversal still reopen it?

Does China PPI strength reflect a temporary war / metals cost shock, or the start of a more persistent producer-price regime?

Does Turkey’s reserve improvement stabilize TRY credibility, or is it too dependent on gold / demand compression to trust?

Is India’s CPI still benign, or does the start of fuel pass-through mark the beginning of a delayed inflation deterioration?

Does Mexico’s IP rebound plus CPI cooling validate a clean soft landing, or is April industrial output just payback after a weak Q1?

Does South Africa manufacturing confirm that the GDP/current-account/mining positives are commodity-flattered rather than genuine domestic recovery?

<<EM_WEEK_BEGIN>>
DATA WINDOW: 31 May 2026 to 5 Jun 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM did not deliver a broad activity collapse, but the week hardened into a dispersion regime rather than a beta regime. India remained the cleanest relative-growth pole, with services, GDP and industrial data still strong, but the RBI separated the strong clean-period starting point from a less benign forward war / energy regime. China shifted from demand-fragile manufacturing to a two-speed profile as services improved, while Taiwan stayed a high-quality export / AI-linked growth case with mild inflation friction. Korea’s strong PMI became less clean once CPI confirmed oil pass-through and core acceleration, moving it into the BoK hawkish-turn cluster.

The negative-quality side broadened. Brazil became the clearest two-signed Hormuz exposure: commodity prices support the nominal trade account and BRL external cushion, but May PMIs show private-sector contraction and cost pressure. South Africa delivered a clean stagflation PMI shock without reserve stress. Turkey remained the dominant EM macro-stability stress node, with GDP, labour and reserves weak, but the final reserve and CPI sequence shifted the base case from accelerating crisis pressure toward conditional stabilization / hold-watch unless FX or reserves deteriorate again.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: ~
Supporting evidence:
Growth dispersion dominated. India services rose to 59.8, GDP beat at 7.8% y/y and IIP held firm under the new base, confirming the strongest EM activity pole, though the RBI downgraded forward FY27 growth. China services improved to 54.4 while manufacturing remained demand-fragile, creating a two-speed profile. Taiwan PMI was strong, but Korea’s PMI quality was inventory-contaminated. Brazil composite PMI fell below 50, South Africa PMI contracted, and Turkey Q1 q/q growth was near stall speed.

Labor: -
Supporting evidence:
The clean labour evidence was mainly Turkey and it deteriorated beneath the headline: unemployment rose only slightly to 8.2%, but employment and labour force both fell sharply and participation dropped. China services employment improved for the first time in four months, but this was not enough to offset Turkey’s domestic-stress signal, and the broader EM tape did not deliver a strong positive labour confirmation.

Inflation: -
Supporting evidence:
Inflation pressure broadened through the energy / cost channel. Korea CPI rose to 3.1% y/y with core at 2.5% and fuel caps suppressing the reported headline. Taiwan CPI moved back above the 2% alert level. South Africa PMI showed the strongest input-cost inflation since July 2022 and output-price inflation at a 46-month high. Brazil PMIs showed elevated cost pressure and IPC-Fipe accelerated modestly. Turkey monthly CPI slowed, but annual inflation still rose and credibility risk remained unresolved. India was the main offset, with services cost pressure easing.

Financial Conditions: -
Supporting evidence:
Turkey’s reserve sequence remained the dominant negative financial-conditions signal: gross and net reserves continued falling, even though the burn rate slowed materially by 29 May. India’s RBI capital-account package showed INR / outflow-management pressure despite strong activity. Korea’s inflation shock raises tightening and KRW-support motives. Brazil’s trade surplus supports the external account and South Africa reserves were benign, but those offsets do not fully neutralize tighter country-specific constraints across the EM map.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
Policy optionality narrowed across most important blocks. Korea moved toward a BoK hawkish-turn candidate after CPI and core acceleration. South Africa’s PMI worsened the SARB trade-off by combining contraction with price pass-through. Brazil’s weak activity is not cleanly easing-friendly because cost pressure remains high and the external account is commodity-price supported. India’s RBI held but raised inflation concerns, cut growth projections and used capital-flow tools. Turkey’s CPI and slower reserve burn support a conditional hold, but cuts remain off the table and hike-tail risk persists if FX / reserves deteriorate. Poland was the exception, staying policy-frozen.

Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Professional Market Commentary

The professional tape framed the official PMI as a stall rather than a collapse: headline exactly at the 50 threshold, consensus-matching, but with weaker demand internals. The key split is production still expanding while new orders and export orders moved below 50; official communication highlighted high-tech and equipment manufacturing as offsets, while wire commentary focused more on weak demand and input-cost pressure.

The scout’s usable hierarchy is: broad manufacturing stall, demand-side softness, export-order contraction, high-tech resilience as a partial sectoral offset, and input-cost pressure still elevated despite some easing.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is not a clean China hard-landing print, but it is a negative-quality activity signal.

Key signals:

headline exactly at 50.0 means the level is stagnant, not outright contractionary
production at 51.2 keeps the supply side positive
new orders at 49.9 and export orders at 48.6 show demand weakening beneath the headline
the export-order reversal matters because the prior China support story relied heavily on external demand / manufacturing resilience
high-tech manufacturing at 52.9 and equipment manufacturing at 52.1 show the policy-favored manufacturing complex still outperforming
raw-material purchase prices eased but remained elevated, so the cost channel has not disappeared

The important macro point is that official China manufacturing remains production-supported but demand-fragile. The headline did not miss consensus, but the subcomponents shift the read toward softer demand quality. This fits the broader China problem: policy-favored supply capacity can look better than end-demand absorption.

State transition: deterioration — headline back to the boundary with new orders and export orders both slipping into contraction.

Context from prior regional live file: China had already moved into a policy-box deterioration regime after weak credit demand and poor household borrowing confirmed that domestic reflation was not self-sustaining. This PMI extends that weakness through the survey channel: production is still holding, but demand and exports are no longer giving the same cushion. HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release reinforces China stimulus expectations, but not in a clean risk-positive way.

Reaction-function map:

PBoC / fiscal support pressure rises because final demand is weak
the input-cost channel complicates broad easing if upstream prices stay elevated
CNH / China beta should not treat the 50.0 headline as stabilization; the export-order detail matters more
high-tech / equipment sectors remain the relative winners inside China, but broad domestic-demand beta remains less convincing

The next verification test is the June PMI / credit combination. A rebound in new orders above 50 with export orders stabilizing would soften the deterioration call. Another weak order print alongside poor credit would deepen the China policy-box problem.

the release therefore overstates clean demand strength if read mechanically

India — Industrial Output YY (Apr)
Release Date: 1 Jun 2026 | Local Time: 12:30 Paris / 16:00 IST
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Industrial Output YY: 4.9% | Prior: 4.1% | Revised: 3.2% | Poll: 3.9% | Surprise: +1.00%

Professional Market Commentary

The professional tape treated the release as both a manufacturing-strength signal and a statistical-reset event. India’s April IIP rose 4.9% y/y under the new 2022-23 base year; manufacturing expanded 6.2%, electricity and gas rose 4.9%, while mining contracted 5.1%. The key caveat is that the new series cannot be directly compared to the old one, while MoSPI’s release emphasized the manufacturing-led nature of the print.

The scout’s core warning is correct: the +1.0pp surprise is not clean because this was the first print of the rebased IIP series. The cyclical signal is firm manufacturing breadth, but the measurement break limits sequential interpretation.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a positive activity print, but the correct interpretation is “new baseline,” not clean acceleration.

Key signals:

headline IIP growth at 4.9% beats poll mechanically
manufacturing at 6.2% is the main positive signal
mining at -5.1% is the clear drag
electricity and gas at 4.9% confirm that the weakness is not broad across industrial buckets
17 of 23 manufacturing groups were positive in the scout detail
motor vehicles, electrical equipment, machinery and infrastructure / construction goods point to investment-linked resilience
the base-year change from 2011-12 to 2022-23 contaminates surprise interpretation and prior comparison

The release reinforces India’s relative activity advantage inside EM, but it should not be over-read as a one-month acceleration. It is the first datapoint in a new statistical regime. The clean macro signal is that manufacturing / capex did not break despite supply-chain and energy-cost pressure.

State transition: stabilization — measurement-qualified; underlying manufacturing momentum looks intact-to-firm, but the series break prevents a clean transition call.

Context from prior regional live file: India had already been a high-quality EM growth story, but recent history added an imported-cost and bottleneck overlay to that resilience. The new IIP print keeps the growth side intact while leaving the inflation / supply-constraint question unresolved. India remains a relative EM growth support, but no longer a frictionless growth-plus-benign-inflation story.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release is INR / India rates-neutral-to-supportive, but not a standalone RBI hawkish trigger.

Reaction-function map:

strong manufacturing breadth supports the RBI’s ability to stay patient
the series break means the upside surprise should not drive front-end repricing mechanically
if GDP and PMIs confirm, India’s growth premium remains intact
if CPI / WPI pass-through rises, the same growth resilience could become more policy-constraining
the new IIP base changes the RBI data map, so May and June prints matter more than the April surprise

The next verification test is India GDP and the next new-series IIP print. Confirmation requires two comparable new-series industrial prints plus service-sector resilience.

Context from prior regional live file: Turkey had already been treated as the EM macro-stability weak link through inflation credibility, reserve vulnerability and policy-rate constraint. wholesale / retail was the weakest sector, while services was the only growing sector
input-cost inflation was the strongest since July 2022
selling-price inflation reached a 46-month high
employment growth was anomalously strong despite weaker demand, likely lagging / vacancy-backfill rather than genuine demand strength
Absa corroborates the front-loading unwind mechanism

The hierarchy is demand contraction first, price pass-through second, employment anomaly third. South Africa’s May PMI kills the “escaped the Hormuz shock” read: growth rolls over just as inflation pressure intensifies.

State transition: reversal — false dawn confirmed; the Jan–Apr expansion phase unwinds as front-loading fades and fuel costs pass through.

Context from prior regional live file: South Africa had previously looked mixed, with better leading indicators offset by PPI and SARB tightening. This PMI resolves the tension negatively: the growth side is now weakening just as price pressure is rising. South Africa moves from mixed resilience to stagflation transmission.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

This worsens the SARB trade-off materially.

Reaction-function map:

weak growth would normally reduce tightening appetite
but input and output price pressure keep SARB constrained
ZAR carry becomes more dependent on global risk appetite and SARB credibility than domestic activity
the print supports the prior SARB tightening logic but makes the macro cost of that stance more visible
South Africa now belongs with Brazil in the front-loading unwind group, but with a cleaner whole-economy stagflation read

The falsification test is a June PMI rebound above 50 driven by genuine new-order growth with stable fuel-price pressure. Without that, South Africa remains a negative-quality EM block.

Brazil — Trade Balance (May)

Professional Market Commentary

Brazil’s May trade surplus beat expectations at roughly $7.8B versus a $7.7B market expectation. The scout frames this as the other side of Brazil’s Hormuz exposure. The same commodity / oil price shock that hurts domestic industry through costs supports the nominal external account through export prices.

the external account is supported by terms of trade, not broad real-demand volume

The hierarchy is price windfall first, volume weakness second, BRL external cushion third. This reconciles the apparent contradiction between a better-than-expected trade surplus and weak PMI export orders: nominal values are supported by prices, while real volumes are soft.

State transition: bifurcation — nominal surplus resilience against contracting real export volumes.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil had already been externally cushioned but domestically policy-constrained. The falsification test is a surplus holding with export volumes recovering, which would improve the real external story. If commodity prices normalize and volumes remain weak, the nominal surplus support would fade.

Taiwan CPI rose to 2.20% y/y, above the 2.10% poll and back above the central bank’s 2% alert level for the first time in more than a year. The scout frames the move as explicitly oil-driven, with food categories also contributing and PPI still well above CPI, indicating unfinished pipeline pressure.

DGBAS commentary in the scout is not alarmist: inflation is described as still mild, with no broad import-inflation signal yet, though June could again exceed 2% on base effects. This makes Taiwan a milder version of the Korea pass-through story rather than a full hawkish shock.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is mild inflation deterioration, not a policy shock.

Key signals:

CPI rose from 1.74% to 2.20%
the print beat consensus by 0.1pp
the 2% alert level was breached
oil / crude-price effects are the main driver
food categories contributed
PPI is running well above CPI, so pipeline pressure has not fully passed through
official commentary still sees inflation as mild and not broad-based

The hierarchy is alert-level breach first, oil-driven nature second, contained broad inflation third. Taiwan joins Korea in confirmed Asian Hormuz CPI pass-through, but the scale and policy relevance are materially milder.

State transition: deterioration — mild inflation; continuation growth. Inflation has moved above the alert threshold, but the pass-through remains contained.

Context from prior regional live file: Taiwan’s PMI had been one of the highest-quality EM activity signals, supported by broad export orders and AI / semis demand. CPI adds mild policy friction to that growth story. Taiwan remains resilient, but no longer a clean growth-only block because the oil channel is now visible in consumer prices.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

This raises the bar for CBC easing, but does not create a strong tightening signal.

Reaction-function map:

CPI above 2% makes policy easing less attractive
PPI-CPI gap means pass-through risk remains
strong PMI plus higher CPI creates a mild stagflation-resilient configuration
TWD support from activity remains, but inflation pressure limits policy optionality
Taiwan is still less hawkish than Korea because pass-through is milder and official commentary remains contained

The falsification test is CPI back below 2% with PPI easing. A sharper CPI breakout or broader import inflation would upgrade the policy relevance.

SIGNAL TENSION CHECK

Main contradiction: EM headline activity is not collapsing, but the forward quality of growth is diverging while inflation and external-financing channels tighten unevenly.
Why it matters: India has strong backward-looking activity but the RBI is cutting forward growth; Turkey has tentative stabilization in monthly CPI and reserve flow but unresolved political and annual-inflation risk; Korea/Taiwan show oil pass-through; Brazil shows the clearest two-signed commodity shock, with external support and domestic stagflation; South Africa shows the cost shock damaging real activity without reserve stress.
Implication: Country dispersion dominates broad EM beta: India is relative-resilient but not yet war-tested, China is two-speed, Korea is hawkish-turn, Taiwan is mild pass-through, Brazil is two-signed Hormuz exposure, South Africa is stagflation-lite, Poland is policy-frozen, and Turkey is active stress with conditional stabilization hints.

5 KEY RELEASES TO DIG INTO

**** Turkey — Net / Gross FX Reserves / CPI / GDP / Labour Cluster (1–5 Jun 2026)
Why it matters: Turkey remains the dominant EM stress node, but the signal has shifted. GDP and labour deteriorated, reserves still fell, yet reserve burn slowed sharply and monthly CPI cooled. Key question: conditional stabilization or temporary calm before TCMB?

**** India — RBI Policy / GDP / Services PMI Cluster (3–5 Jun 2026)
Why it matters: India is the cleanest EM resilience case, but the week separates strong clean-period data from a deteriorating forward war regime. RBI’s FY27 growth downgrade and capital-account measures matter more than the GDP headline alone.

**** South Korea — CPI Growth MM / YY (2 Jun 2026)
Why it matters: Clearest Asia inflation pass-through event. CPI is at a 26-month high, core accelerated, and fuel caps suppress the headline, turning Korea from clean growth outperformer into a BoK hawkish-turn candidate.

**** South Africa — Standard Bank Whole Economy PMI / Reserves (3–5 Jun 2026)
Why it matters: The PMI is a clean stagflation print, while reserves are benign. This distinction matters: ZAR stress is real-economy / SARB-trade-off driven, not external-buffer driven.

*** Brazil — Industrial Output / Services-Composite PMI / Trade Balance Cluster (3 Jun 2026)
Why it matters: Brazil is the clearest two-signed Hormuz case: April hard activity was commodity / extraction-supported, May soft data rolled into private-sector contraction, and the trade surplus beat only because export prices rose while volumes fell. Key for BRL / BCB interpretation.

RED TEAM QUESTIONS FOR JGM OR SECOND PASS SCOUT

For Turkey, do slower reserve burn and lower monthly CPI now justify a hold base case, or is political / FX risk still enough to keep the hike tail alive?

For India, should the 7.8% GDP beat be discounted almost entirely as a last-clean-read, or does it still raise the structural resilience prior?

For Brazil, is the trade-price windfall enough to keep BRL supported despite composite contraction, or does domestic stagflation dominate the currency/rates map?

For Korea and Taiwan, is Asian oil CPI pass-through now broad enough to change central-bank reaction functions, or is Korea the only real hawkish case?

For South Africa, is the stress correctly located in PMI stagflation rather than reserves, or are reserves masking a later external-risk problem?

For China, does services strength overturn the demand-fragility thesis, or does it merely create a two-speed economy with goods still weak?

What would falsify the current EM dispersion map: India resilient but war-untested, China two-speed, Korea hawkish-turn, Taiwan mild pass-through, Brazil two-signed Hormuz exposure, South Africa stagflation-lite, Turkey conditional stabilization?
