<<EM_WEEK_BEGIN>>
DATA WINDOW: 25 May 2026 to 29 May 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM did not deliver a broad activity rollover; the week’s signal was dispersion under a tighter inflation-policy constraint. North Asia remained the positive pole through Taiwan’s AI/electronics industrial cycle, while South Africa’s leading indicator improved and Brazil’s external accounts / GDP mechanics offered support. But the dominant regime shift came from policy and prices: Brazil IPCA-15 kept consumer-stage inflation sticky despite wholesale relief, South Africa moved from pipeline inflation to an actual SARB hike, and Korea’s BoK hold became hawkish via dissents, forecasts, KRW sensitivity and a higher-rate bias. Friday’s tracker-only releases add potentially important offsets — Poland CPI disinflation, weaker Korea activity/retail, Brazil GDP resilience — but they remain unbuilt pending scout, so the frozen analytical signal is EM resilience with a rising policy constraint, not clean reflation and not clean disinflation.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: ~
Supporting evidence:
Growth was resilient but uneven. Taiwan industrial output remained very strong despite y/y base normalization, South Africa’s leading indicator improved materially, and Brazil’s external accounts / later GDP intake supported the activity cushion. But Korea’s Friday industrial output and retail sales were weaker on the mechanical feed and remain unbuilt, while Poland retail sales showed a real sequential soft patch. Net signal: no EM demand collapse, but highly dispersed and not a clean acceleration.

Labor: ~
Supporting evidence:
Labor evidence was limited. Poland unemployment matched consensus at 6.0%, consistent with stable labor conditions and preventing the weak retail print from becoming a recession signal. No broader EM labor block was built, so the labor bucket remains neutral rather than regime-defining.

Inflation: -
Supporting evidence:
Inflation pressure deteriorated where it mattered most for policy. Brazil IPCA-15 slowed m/m but beat consensus, accelerated y/y to 4.64%, and showed firmer core/services pressure underneath transport relief. South Africa PPI surprised sharply higher, confirming petroleum-linked pipeline inflation ahead of SARB. Brazil IGP-M offered wholesale stabilization, and Poland CPI flash later suggested disinflation mechanically, but the built week’s dominant inflation signal remains adverse.

Financial Conditions: -
Supporting evidence:
Financial conditions tightened through the policy channel. BoK’s hold became hawkish through dissents, forecast upgrades, KRW sensitivity and a higher-rate bias. SARB hiked 25bp and moved into pre-emptive inflation-defense mode. Brazil’s strong FDI quality and external-account improvement supported external financing, but not enough to offset a broader shift toward more constrained policy reaction functions.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
Policy constraint rose materially. South Africa shifted from inflation risk into active tightening after the PPI/SARB sequence; Korea’s easing-cycle narrative was effectively closed by a hawkish BoK reaction-function shift; Brazil’s Copom easing path stayed vulnerable to sticky consumer inflation despite upstream relief. The week therefore tightened the EM policy map even as activity did not collapse.

MONDAY 25 MAY 2026

Poland — Retail Sales / Retail Sales Constant Price (Apr)
Release Date: 25 May 2026 | Local Time: 09:30
Importance: **

Reuters Data

Retail Sales YY: 2,8% | Prior: 9,8% | Poll: 3,0% | Surprise: -0,20%
Retail Sales Cons Price: 1,3% | Prior: 8,7% | Poll: 3,0% | Surprise: -1,70%

Professional Market Commentary

The tape frames the April retail report as a sharp moderation from an exceptionally strong March rather than a clean consumer rollover. The official/statistical framing in the scout shows real retail sales +1.3% y/y, below the 3.0% poll, after +8.7% in March; it also flags a -0.8% m/m real decline and Jan–Apr cumulative real sales of +3.4% y/y, keeping the YTD demand trend broadly stable.

Accessible commentary is consistent with the “base-effect give-back” read. The important nuance is that the sequential contraction should not be dismissed entirely.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is an optical deterioration with a genuine soft patch underneath.

Key signals:

the y/y deceleration is mechanically large because March was unusually strong
the real-sales miss versus poll is meaningful, but not enough to declare a demand break
Jan–Apr real sales at +3.4% y/y keep the YTD demand trend broadly stable
the -0.8% m/m real decline is the main non-benign detail
Easter timing / base effects likely exaggerate the deterioration
the gap between nominal +2.8% y/y and real +1.3% y/y is consistent with still-positive consumer-price deflation pressure rather than pure volume collapse

The scout’s divergence check is the right hierarchy: the market narrative can lean too benign if it only says “mean reversion,” but the raw headline can also look too weak if read without base effects. The useful signal is continuation with mild sequential softness, not a Polish consumer recession.

State transition: false dawn — conditional, inverted. The weak headline overstates deterioration just as March overstated strength.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland had previously been treated as relatively resilient within EM, with softer GDP and confirmed inflation preventing a clean dovish read. April retail sales add a consumption-softness flag but do not yet break that resilience because the YTD trend remains stable. The regime remains domestic-demand moderation rather than outright deterioration.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: marginally dovish for the NBP margin, but too base-distorted to carry policy weight alone.

Rates / FX implication: PLN does not get a strong negative macro signal from this release because the y/y collapse is optical; however, a second consecutive negative real m/m print would start to validate a real-income / consumption squeeze.

Next verification test: May retail sales and Poland flash CPI. If retail weakness persists while CPI remains sticky, Poland shifts toward a weaker-consumption / constrained-policy mix.

the signal points to H2 activity improvement, but not yet to a confirmed hard-data acceleration

Brazil — IPCA-15 Mid-Month CPI / IPCA-15 YY (May)
Release Date: 27 May 2026 | Local Time: 14:00

Reuters Data

Professional Market Commentary

IBGE reported IPCA-15 at 0.62% in May, down from 0.89% in April, but with the 12-month rate accelerating to 4.64% from 4.37%. Food and beverages and housing were the main positive contributors, while transportation was the only negative group.

The scout’s professional tape flags the key under-the-hood issue: transport disinflation masks persistence in core / services. The named StoneX read cited in the scout frames the print as broader and more persistent, with initial energy-linked pressures beginning to diffuse into other components. Pantheon’s one-line public read also characterizes May inflation pressure as broad-based.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is not a clean cooling print even though the headline m/m rate fell from April.

Key signals:

headline IPCA-15 slowed m/m, but still beat consensus
12-month IPCA-15 accelerated from 4.37% to 4.64%
food and housing carried the headline contribution
transportation was negative, mainly diluting the headline through fuel reversal
electricity tariff effects added a discrete housing boost
the core/services symmetry identified in the scout is the hawkish detail
the headline cooling and the underlying persistence point in opposite directions

The analytical hierarchy is: underlying persistence first, headline transport relief second, tariff artifact third. The release does not say Brazil inflation is re-accelerating mechanically through fuel anymore; it says the earlier energy shock may now be entering broader consumer categories while fuel provides a temporary offset.

State transition: continuation — conditional. Brazil remains in sticky-inflation / constrained-easing mode, with the composition more hawkish than the headline m/m decline.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil had already moved from “growth resilient, inflation-capped easing” toward “sticky prices with uneven activity” after weak services volumes and firm inflation pressure. IPCA-15 confirms that the inflation constraint remains binding even after the improvement in external accounts. The regime remains a Brazil-specific stagflation calibration rather than a clean disinflation or clean slowdown case.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: hawkish under the hood for Copom, but not a standalone hike signal.

Rates / FX implication: the print challenges an overly smooth Selic easing path because the services/core details are not cooling cleanly. BRL can still benefit from carry and improved external financing, but the domestic rates story remains capped by persistent inflation rather than liberated by weaker transport prices.

Next verification test: next IPCA / IPCA-15 services and core. A services/core rollback below roughly the recent firm pace would validate the upstream-cooling story; another firm services print would make the second-round transmission concern harder to fade.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: SARB is now in inflation-defense mode, but the path should still be described conditionally.

Rates / FX implication: ZAR gets carry support and credibility support, but the same shock weakens the real-income and growth-quality story. SAGB front-end should price a higher probability of further tightening if May/June CPI confirms food/fuel pass-through.

Next verification test: May CPI, PPI persistence, food-price transmission and ZAR/oil behavior. A fast energy normalization could turn this into a one-and-done hike; persistent oil / food pressure keeps additional tightening live.

<<EM_WEEK_BEGIN>>
DATA WINDOW: 18 May 2026 to 22 May 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM bifurcated sharply over 18–22 May rather than delivering a single beta signal. China was the clearest deterioration case, with retail sales near-stalling, investment contracting and the PBoC refusing to validate broad LPR easing. South Africa and Poland shifted into inflation-constraint territory, with South Africa’s CPI jump and Poland’s PPI/core inflation mix overriding softer labor or activity data. India and Taiwan remained the positive side of the tape, but with different quality: India preserved strong headline growth through services while manufacturing/export orders weakened, whereas Taiwan remained the clean AI/export-cycle outlier with export orders and labor still supportive.

Turkey improved on trade but remained reserve-fragile, while Mexico moved into a less-bad growth / sticky-core inflation mix after stronger IGAE and an upward GDP revision, but without a genuine disinflation clearance. The final EM regime is therefore dispersion-led: China policy-box deterioration; South Africa/Poland hawkish-hold constraint; India false-dawn resilience; Taiwan AI-export outperformance; Turkey fragile stabilization; Mexico Banxico cycle-end support rather than renewed easing.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: ~
Supporting evidence:
China’s activity block was decisively negative, with retail sales at 0,2% y/y, urban investment at -1,6% YTD y/y and industrial output missing consensus. Brazil’s IBC-Br cooled, Poland’s industrial output normalized lower after March, and South Africa’s retail strength was backward-looking. Offsetting that, India’s composite PMI stayed very high at 58,1, Taiwan export orders remained strong at 48,1% y/y, and Mexico’s IGAE surprised materially to the upside. The EM growth signal is therefore bifurcated, not uniformly weak.

Labor: ~
Supporting evidence:
Labor evidence was limited and mixed. China’s urban unemployment improved to 5,2%, but the activity deterioration dominated. Poland employment remained negative at -0,9% y/y while wage growth slowed more than expected, easing wage-pressure risk but confirming soft corporate labor demand. Taiwan’s adjusted jobless rate edged down to 3,34%, confirming resilience. The period did not produce a clean EM labor regime shift.

Inflation: -
Supporting evidence:
South Africa CPI rose from 3,1% to 4,0% with both goods and services acceleration, breaking the benign SARB disinflation path. Poland net inflation rose to 3,0% and PPI surprised sharply at 1,9% y/y versus a -0,1% poll, confirming pipeline pressure. Mexico’s headline half-month inflation looked softer, but the source tape identifies the improvement as seasonal and still constrained by sticky core/services. Inflation risk worsened across the policy-relevant EM subset.

Financial Conditions: ~
Supporting evidence:
Turkey’s trade balance improved from -11,22B to -8,5B and gross FX reserves rose, but net FX reserves fell, keeping reserve credibility fragile. Taiwan and Mexico retained FX support from export/activity resilience and sticky-rate differentials, while CNH stayed vulnerable to weak growth and constrained policy. Financial conditions were therefore not uniformly tightening, but the quality of stabilization was uneven and country-specific.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
The PBoC held 1Y and 5Y LPR unchanged despite the weak China hard-data package, confirming policy support is constrained and likely targeted rather than broad-rate-led. SARB easing optionality was effectively closed by the CPI jump. Poland’s PPI/core mix capped NBP easing despite softer wages and output. Banxico received support for a hold/cycle-end stance from less-bad activity and sticky core. Across EM, policy space narrowed more than it opened.

C. FULL RELEASE ARCHIVE

MONDAY 18 MAY 2026

China Mainland — Industrial Output / Retail Sales / Urban Investment / Urban Unemployment (Apr)

Release Date: 18 May 2026 | Local Time: 04:00
Importance: ****

Reuters Data

Industrial Output YY: 4,1% | Prior: 5,7% | Poll: 5,9% | Surprise: -1,80%
Retail Sales YY: 0,2% | Prior: 1,7% | Poll: 2,0% | Surprise: -1,80%
Urban Investment (YTD) YY: -1,6% | Prior: 1,7% | Poll: 1,6% | Surprise: -3,20%
Unemp Rate Urban Area: 5,2% | Prior: 5,4%

Professional Market Commentary

The scout tape frames the release as the first hard-data confirmation that China’s domestic-demand leg has broken below the prior false-dawn stabilization path: retail sales nearly stalled, investment contracted, and industrial production missed sharply, while the unemployment-rate improvement looked insufficient to offset the broader activity deterioration.

The professional tape and wire framing put the emphasis on weak domestic demand, property drag, external-risk transmission and export front-loading rather than a clean domestic recovery.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is the cleanest China deterioration block of the week so far.

Key signals:

Retail sales at 0,2% y/y are the dominant macro signal. This is not merely a soft consumption print; it is effectively a stall in nominal retail activity.
Urban investment falling -1,6% YTD y/y is the second signal and confirms that weakness is not isolated to household consumption.
Industrial output at 4,1% y/y still grows, but the miss versus 5,9% consensus breaks the prior “production resilient / domestic demand incomplete” balance.
The urban unemployment-rate improvement to 5,2% is not enough to stabilize the block because the activity and demand variables dominate the signal hierarchy.
The internal hierarchy is therefore: consumption stall first, investment contraction second, production miss third, labor-rate optics fourth.

The release converts China from “uneven but supported by exports and services” into a demand-side deterioration case. The prior China support story relied on export resilience and selective services strength; this hard-data package shows the domestic side is not absorbing the external shock.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: China had already shifted from export-supported stabilization toward policy-box deterioration after weak credit demand and fragile private borrowing. The April activity package confirms that final domestic demand has not followed the export impulse. The regime is now weaker domestic demand inside a constrained policy mix.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the release increases pressure for policy support, but not necessarily via immediate rate cuts.

Rates / FX implication: CGBs can retain a support-expectation bias, while CNH remains vulnerable because the data are not growth-positive and the policy response is still constrained. China equities should keep a split between policy-supported / AI-linked sectors and domestic-demand-sensitive sectors.

The critical point is that the PBoC cannot treat this as a normal cyclical slowdown if LPR and liquidity settings remain unchanged. The next verification test is fiscal execution, local-government special-bond deployment, consumption subsidies, and May retail / credit data. If May retail remains near zero and credit stays weak, China becomes the clearest EM demand-side deterioration case rather than just a policy-support candidate.

Release Date: 18 May 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

IBC-BR Economic Activity: -0,7 | Prior: 0,6 | Poll: -0,2 | Surprise: -0,5

Professional Market Commentary

Reuters framed Brazil’s March activity print as a sharp monthly fall inside a still-positive Q1: the IBC-Br proxy fell 0,7% m/m versus a 0,2% expected decline, while Q1 activity still rose 1,3% q/q. The report also noted broad sector weakness in March, including services, but kept the interpretation two-sided because January and February were strong enough to preserve quarterly momentum.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a cooling signal, but not a Brazil regime break.

Key signals:

The monthly miss is meaningful because the decline was worse than consensus.
The Q1 context dilutes the signal: the quarter still expanded strongly after a firm January-February sequence.
The March weakness fits the prior services-volume deterioration rather than contradicting it.
The policy signal is not straightforwardly dovish because Brazil’s inflation backdrop remains too sticky for the BCB to accelerate easing.

The right hierarchy is: March stall first, Q1 resilience second, inflation constraint third. The activity print lowers the quality of Brazil’s growth read, but it does not restore clean easing optionality.

State transition: no material change — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil had already moved from “growth resilient, inflation-capped easing” toward “sticky prices with uneven activity” after weak services volumes and firm inflation pressure. IBC-Br confirms the uneven-activity leg but does not overturn Q1 resilience. Brazil remains a stagflationary calibration case rather than a clean slowdown case.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the print complicates Copom calibration but does not create a standalone dovish pivot.

Rates / FX implication: BRL loses some clean growth support at the margin, but carry and Q1 resilience still prevent a pure bearish activity read. DI receivers get some tactical support from weaker activity, but sticky inflation and services-price rigidity cap the move.

The next verification test is May IPCA services and April services volumes. If services volumes remain weak while services inflation remains sticky, Brazil becomes a cleaner LatAm stagflation sub-case. If activity rebounds and inflation remains firm, the hawkish-output-gap read returns.

Poland — Net Inflation (Apr 2026)

Release Date: 18 May 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Net Inflation YY: 3 | Prior: 2,7 | Poll: 3 | Surprise: 0

Professional Market Commentary

NBP confirmed that inflation net of food and energy prices was 3,0% y/y in April. The scout tape framed this as a confirmation rather than a surprise: the policy issue is the direction of underlying inflation after the prior CPI acceleration.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is not a surprise print, but it matters because of the direction.

Key signals:

Core / net inflation accelerated from 2,70% to 3,00%.
The print matched consensus, so the market event is not the surprise; it is the confirmation of re-acceleration.
The move reinforces the message from final CPI: Poland’s inflation mix is no longer easing cleanly.
This matters more after the prior GDP slowdown because it blocks a simple “growth softer, NBP can ease” interpretation.

Poland’s macro mix is now: resilient but slowing activity, manageable external accounts, and re-firming underlying inflation. The external side is not the binding constraint; core inflation is.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland had already been framed as a resilient CEE economy with the policy discussion constrained by inflation and energy sensitivity. Final CPI kept that constraint in place after the Q1 GDP slowdown, and the net-inflation print confirms the core side of the same story. Poland remains resilient, but the inflation-growth mix is less benign.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: no NBP easing validation.

Rates / FX implication: PLN can retain support from a higher-for-longer NBP profile, while POLGB front-end easing expectations should remain capped. The print is not large enough to create a new hawkish shock, but it confirms that March easing was not the start of a smooth cutting cycle.

The next verification test is May CPI flash and May core. A renewed core deceleration would stabilize the read; a move toward the upper target band would move Poland further into EM inflation-channel deterioration.

The LPR hold is more important because it follows the weak 18 May hard-data package.

The policy rate signal did not respond to retail-sales near-stagnation.
The 5Y LPR hold means no immediate broad mortgage-rate relief through the benchmark channel.
The 1Y LPR hold signals no broad credit-cost easing for corporate borrowers.
This confirms that the policy reaction function is constrained by bank margins, yuan stability and imported-cost risk rather than domestic demand alone.

The policy hierarchy is now clear: fiscal and targeted credit support matter more than LPR cuts. The PBoC is not ignoring the slowdown, but it is choosing not to validate a broad monetary easing impulse through the LPR channel.

State transition: continuation — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: China had already moved into a tighter policy box after prices rose while credit demand weakened. The LPR hold confirms that the central bank is not responding mechanically to weaker domestic demand. The regime remains support-biased but constrained rather than outright easing-led.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: policy support expectations shift away from broad rate cuts and toward fiscal execution, targeted lending, local-government bond deployment and administrative demand support.

Rates / FX implication: CGB downside-yield pressure can persist because activity is weak, but CNH does not get clean support from the hold if growth data keep deteriorating. The hold is not hawkish in a conventional sense; it is “tightening by inaction” relative to the domestic-demand shock.

The next verification test is not the next LPR alone. It is whether May credit, retail sales and fiscal disbursement show that targeted policy is offsetting the hard-data deterioration.

Reuters Data

Professional Market Commentary

Stats SA’s April CPI release shows the annual inflation rate rising to 4,0%, with goods inflation up to 3,4% from 1,8% and services inflation up to 4,6% from 4,2%. Reuters framed the jump as important for the SARB reaction function, with market attention shifting toward whether the inflation acceleration increases the probability of a rate hike rather than additional easing.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is the highest-quality inflation shock in the current scout scope.

Key signals:

Headline CPI rose from 3,1% to 4,0%.
The monthly move of 1,1% confirms a large sequential price impulse.
Goods inflation accelerated sharply, consistent with the fuel / import-cost channel.
Services inflation also rose, which prevents treating this as a pure first-round fuel print.
Core / underlying pressure matters more than the headline surprise because the surprise itself was only +0,10pp.

The hierarchy is: headline jump first, goods acceleration second, services rise third, policy implication fourth. The print breaks the benign SARB disinflation track and tests the look-through doctrine.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: South Africa had previously been a conditional-stabilization case, with activity and commodity buffers offset by fuel-shock risk and uneven domestic demand. April CPI validates the cost-risk side of that setup. The regime shifts from benign inflation support toward policy-constrained inflation transmission.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the SARB easing window is effectively closed for now, and hike-risk language becomes more credible if May CPI extends the acceleration.

Rates / FX implication: SAGB front-end pricing should remove residual easing comfort. ZAR can receive relative support from a more restrictive SARB reaction function, but that support is fragile if the inflation shock damages real incomes or global risk sentiment.

The next verification test is May CPI and fuel pass-through. If goods inflation stabilizes and services do not broaden, SARB can keep the look-through doctrine alive. If services and expectations follow headline higher, the reaction function shifts toward active tightening risk.

The macro read remains AI/export-cycle resilience, not broad EM domestic demand.

State transition: continuation — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Taiwan had already been identified as one of the cleanest North Asia AI-cycle confirmation signals, with PMI strength reinforcing export and semiconductor resilience. The S&P Global / HSBC flash release showed India’s composite PMI easing only marginally to 58,1 from 58,2, with services at 58,9 and manufacturing PMI at 54,3. The official release emphasized that service providers outperformed manufacturers, while total new orders, international sales, employment and business activity rose at weaker rates. It also highlighted the weakest expansion in new export orders in 19 months and cited competitive pressures, challenging demand conditions, travel disruption and the Middle East war as factors weighing on manufacturing demand.

The scout tape correctly frames the release as a headline-resilient but internally weaker India print: services still hold the composite at a very high level, while manufacturing orders and export orders show clear external-channel stress.

Manufacturing PMI at 54,3 missed consensus and softened versus April.
Manufacturing new orders and export orders are the real deterioration signal, not the composite headline.
Inventory building is a key sustaining variable: manufacturers continued stockpiling, with purchases rising at the fastest pace in three months and finished-goods stocks rising for a second consecutive month.
Input-price pressure rose, while output-charge inflation was softer, implying some margin absorption rather than clean pass-through.

The hierarchy is: services resilience first, manufacturing export-channel deterioration second, inventory front-loading third, margin-pressure risk fourth. India is still the EM growth-quality outperformer, but the release weakens the “clean resilience” interpretation because the manufacturing engine is being propped up by inventories while orders slow.

State transition: false dawn — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: India had previously been the cleanest EM domestic-demand outperformer, with services strength offsetting weaker manufacturing and cost pressure. May flash PMIs preserve the high-level growth story but show that external demand and inventory dynamics are now degrading the quality of the signal. India remains resilient, but the resilience is less clean than the composite headline suggests.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the RBI does not receive a clean dovish signal from the composite, but the manufacturing internals warn against extrapolating India exceptionalism mechanically.

Rates / FX implication: INR remains supported by relative growth quality, especially versus China demand deterioration and Turkey external fragility. The rates read is mixed: weaker manufacturing supports the growth-slowdown argument, but input-cost pressure and services resilience keep the RBI from leaning aggressively dovish.

The next verification test is June PMI. If inventories continue to rise while export orders soften further, the composite should catch down. If export orders recover and inventories normalize, India revalidates the resilient-growth regime.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland had previously looked stronger on hard activity after a sharp March industrial rebound. This is the most important Poland release of 21 May.

Key signals:

PPI surprised by +2,0pp versus Reuters poll.
The prior was revised from -0,8% to +1,2%, meaning the producer-price inflection had already started before April.
The y/y rate moved firmly into positive territory.
The m/m rise of 0,5% confirms sequential pipeline pressure.
This aligns with the earlier net-inflation acceleration and weakens any dovish interpretation of slower wages or softer industrial output.

The hierarchy is: PPI inflection first, prior revision second, interaction with core inflation third. Poland’s problem is not demand overheating; it is producer/core inflation pressure arriving while activity is only moderate.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland had already moved from benign disinflation toward an inflation-constrained policy setup after CPI and net inflation. April PPI adds the producer-price channel and confirms that the inflation problem is no longer only consumer-core optics. The regime is now mixed growth with a more binding pipeline-inflation constraint.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: this is the release that keeps NBP easing off the table despite weaker wages and softer industrial output.

Rates / FX implication: PLN should treat the block as supportive through rate-differential logic, but not because growth is improving. POLGB front-end easing expectations should remain capped; the curve can flatten if markets emphasize policy constraint over activity softness.

The next verification test is May CPI/PPI and NBP communication. If PPI stays positive and core remains near 3%, the policy debate moves from “cutting cycle paused” toward “hawkish hold with hike-risk language.”

Turkey — Gross FX Reserves / Net FX Reserves (W/E 15 May 2026)

Release Date: 21 May 2026 | Local Time: 13:30
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Gross FX Reserves: 61,23B | Prior: 60,56B
Net FX Reserves: 52,12B | Prior: 55,02B

Professional Market Commentary

CBRT’s international-reserves page carried the weekly 15 May 2026 data release, while public market trackers show gross foreign-exchange reserves rising to roughly US$61,2bn from US$60,6bn in the prior week. The scout tape emphasized that gross FX accumulation continued, but the final Reuters mechanical base adds the key missing counterpoint: net FX reserves fell from 55,02B to 52,12B.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a composition-over-headline Turkey block, but the composition is mixed, not cleanly positive.

Key signals:

Gross FX reserves rose by roughly 0,67B.
Net FX reserves fell by roughly 2,90B.
The scout tape’s gold-valuation argument helps explain weakness in total reserves, but the Reuters net-reserve line prevents a clean “reserve rebuild intact” conclusion.
Gross FX accumulation is still useful, but net reserves are the cleaner credibility metric for TRY stabilization.
The correct interpretation is therefore: gross buffer slightly better, net buffer weaker, reserve-rebuild quality still fragile.

The hierarchy is: net reserve deterioration first, gross FX accumulation second, gold valuation third. Turkey remains in reserve-defense stabilization, but the quality of the reserve signal is weaker than the gross headline alone implies.

State transition: continuation with weaker quality — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Turkey had already been the clearest EM financial-stability stress point after CPI, weak PMI and reserve drawdown. The latest reserves data do not show a renewed gross FX collapse, but the net-reserve decline keeps the credibility constraint alive. Turkey remains defensive-stabilization rather than clean reserve-rebuild.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: CBRT cannot treat this as a clean easing-validating reserve print.

Rates / FX implication: TRY stability remains conditional on continued tight policy and sustained net-reserve rebuilding. Gross FX stabilization helps at the margin, but the net-reserve decline keeps long-TRY carry exposed to any renewed external shock or domestic FX demand.

The next verification test is the 28 May reserves release for week-ended 22 May. If gross and net reserves both rebuild, Turkey moves toward stabilization. If gross holds but net falls again, the market should discount the reserve buffer more aggressively.

FRIDAY 22 MAY 2026

Turkey — Trade Balance (Apr 2026)

Release Date: 22 May 2026 | Local Time: 09:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Trade Balance: -8,5 | Prior: -11,22

Professional Market Commentary

The Trade Ministry’s April foreign-trade data showed exports up 22,3% y/y to USD25,4bn and imports up 3,1% to USD33,9bn, leaving a USD8,5bn deficit. That matches the final Reuters mechanical direction: a clear narrowing versus March’s USD11,22bn deficit. The scout tape frames the print as a real export rebound, but with a two-handed caveat because the January-April deficit still widened versus the same period last year.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is Turkey’s best external-account print in the current week, but not a full external-stability clearance.

Key signals:

The deficit narrowed from -11,22B to -8,5B.
Export growth was strong enough to reverse the March deterioration.
Import growth was limited, which improved the coverage ratio.
Ex-energy / ex-gold detail in the scout tape shows a much healthier underlying trade structure than the headline deficit implies.
The cumulative Jan-Apr deficit remains worse than last year, so the monthly improvement does not erase the year-to-date external gap.

The hierarchy is: April export rebound first, underlying ex-energy improvement second, YTD deterioration third. Turkey’s external account is not collapsing, but the reserve and trade blocks together still describe a fragile stabilization rather than a clean recovery.

State transition: improvement — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Turkey had previously been dominated by reserve-defense stress, inflation pressure and policy credibility risk. The April trade balance offsets part of that pressure by showing the export channel can rebound while imports remain contained. The regime improves from acute external deterioration toward fragile stabilization.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the trade print is TRY-supportive at the margin, especially after the gross-FX-reserve stabilization, but it does not remove the need for tight CBRT policy.

Rates / FX implication: TRY carry gets a better external-account backdrop, but the net-reserve decline from the previous block prevents a clean bullish signal. Turkey remains a carry-and-credibility trade, not a restored external-balance trade.

The next verification test is May trade and the 28 May reserve release. If May reverses because of holiday effects or energy costs while net reserves decline again, the April improvement becomes a one-month relief print. If trade and net reserves both improve, Turkey moves toward a more credible stabilization bucket.

The sectoral caveat is K-shaped: AI-linked / service resilience is stronger than non-tech industrial breadth.

Mexico — 1st Half-Month Core Inflation / Headline Inflation (May 2026)

Release Date: 22 May 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

1st Half-Mth Core Infl MM: 0,13 | Prior: 0,18 | Poll: 0,17 | Surprise: -0,04

Professional Market Commentary

The Reuters poll had expected Mexico headline inflation to ease to 4,13% y/y in the first half of May, with prices down 0,15% over the half-month. The actual mechanical print was close to that expectation: headline prices fell 0,16% half-month, while core rose only 0,13%, below the 0,17% poll. The scout tape adds the key composition: headline deceleration was driven by electricity/tariff seasonality, while core and services remained sticky.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a false-dawn disinflation print.

Key signals:

Headline half-month inflation was slightly more negative than expected.
Core was softer than expected on a m/m basis.
The headline improvement is heavily seasonal, driven by electricity / hot-season tariff adjustments.
Core remains the policy variable, not the headline print.
Services inflation remains the sticky component, limiting the dovish read.

The hierarchy is: seasonal headline decline first, core softness second, services stickiness third. This print helps Banxico at the margin, but it does not prove structural disinflation.

State transition: false dawn — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Mexico had already been a sticky-inflation / weak-growth policy trade-off. The first-half May inflation print reduces near-term headline pressure, but the composition keeps the core-services constraint alive. Mexico remains a cycle-done / sticky-core case rather than a renewed easing case.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the release supports a hold rather than a new easing impulse.

Rates / FX implication: MXN can stay supported because the inflation composition does not justify renewed dovish repricing, while the activity data are less bad. Local rates should fade a pure headline-disinflation rally unless core follow-through improves.

The next verification test is the second half of May inflation print. If core falls below 4% y/y and services cool, Banxico gets more genuine easing optionality. If headline remains soft but core/services stay sticky, the market should keep pricing a high-for-longer Banxico path.

SIGNAL TENSION CHECK

Main contradiction: EM is bifurcating rather than converging. China is demand deterioration; South Africa and Poland are inflation-channel constraint; India is headline resilience with weaker internals; Turkey is improving on trade but fragile on net reserves; Taiwan is AI-export immunity; Mexico is less-bad growth with sticky core inflation.

Why it matters: Broad EM beta is less useful than country-specific constraint mapping.

Implication: Keep EM in buckets: China policy-box deterioration; South Africa / Poland hawkish-hold constraint; India false-dawn resilience; Turkey fragile stabilization; Mexico sticky-core / less-bad growth; Taiwan AI-export outperformance.

3 KEY RELEASES TO DIG INTO

China Activity Data Complex (18 May)
Why it matters: Retail sales at 0,2%, investment contraction and industrial-output miss make this the cleanest demand-side deterioration print of the week. It directly challenges the prior China stabilization narrative and makes the PBoC / fiscal response the central question.
South Africa CPI (20 May)
Why it matters: The jump from 3,1% to 4,0% with goods and services acceleration is the clearest inflation-channel confirmation. It effectively closes SARB easing optionality unless May data reverses.
Mexico Activity / Inflation Cluster (22 May)
Why it matters: GDP and IGAE show a less-bad growth path, while first-half May inflation looks softer at headline level but still compositionally sticky. This is the cleanest Banxico reaction-function block of the week.

<<EM_WEEK_BEGIN>>
DATA WINDOW: 11 May 2026 to 15 May 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM shifted from conditional stabilization / false dawn toward a clearer stagflationary-dispersion map: China delivered the week’s sharpest policy-box signal, with cost-led CPI/PPI reflation followed by collapsing credit demand; India moved from benign CPI optics to a measured wholesale-input shock; Brazil combined sticky inflation, resilient retail and then a sharp services-volume contraction; Turkey stayed in external-defence mode; Mexico remained the hard-activity laggard. The offset was not absent: Korea confirmed the AI-export positive pole, Poland retained external-account resilience despite softer GDP and confirmed inflation, and South Africa remained compositionally cushioned by metals rather than broad domestic acceleration.

The resulting regime is not synchronized EM deterioration, but country-specific constraint tightening. The week’s dominant macro message is “prices and policy constraints up, domestic demand quality uneven”: central banks have less room to ease where imported/pipeline inflation is visible, while weak credit, services-volume softness and external-financing stress prevent a clean growth upgrade.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: ~
Supporting evidence:
China’s credit block was outright growth-negative, with new yuan loans contracting, TSF missing sharply and household credit weakness confirming poor private-demand transmission. Mexico industrial output extended a weak manufacturing / construction regime, Brazil retail was strong but services volumes fell sharply, Poland GDP slowed but remained resilient, South Africa stabilized only selectively, and Korea exports remained the clear positive outlier through semiconductors.

Labor: ~
Supporting evidence:
India unemployment matched poll at 5.2% and did not show labor overheating, but LFPR softness and weaker female participation reduced the quality of the labor read. The week did not provide a broad EM labor regime signal; the binding macro tension came from inflation / credit / external accounts rather than employment.

Inflation: -
Supporting evidence:
India WPI at 8.30% converted CPI pass-through risk into a measured wholesale shock; China PPI jumped to 2.8% y/y before credit confirmed weak demand; Brazil IPCA moved closer to the top of the target range with food / health pressure; Poland final CPI confirmed 3.2% y/y with core pressure firming. The inflation signal is cost-led and policy-constraining, not demand-led overheating.

Financial Conditions: -
Supporting evidence:
Turkey’s current-account deficit widened to USD 9.672bn with reserve-defence still the dominant regime, even after a one-week reserve rebound. China’s liquidity backdrop failed to translate into private credit creation. Brazil’s rates path became harder after IPCA / retail / services divergence, while Mexico’s weak activity sits alongside Banxico credibility and ratings constraints.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
The week narrowed easing room across several EMs without delivering synchronized growth strength. PBoC support is constrained by cost-led reflation; RBI can wait but now faces hard WPI pipeline evidence; BCB easing is capped by sticky inflation despite weaker services volumes; CBRT remains in external-defence mode; NBP cannot read softer GDP as cleanly dovish while CPI/core remain firm.

C. FULL RELEASE ARCHIVE

MONDAY 11 MAY 2026

China (Mainland) — CPI / PPI Inflation Complex (Apr)
Release Date: 11 May 2026 | Local Time: 03:30
Importance: ****

Reuters Data

PPI YY: 2.8% | Prior: 0.5% | Poll: 1.6% | Surprise: 1.20%
CPI YY: 1.2% | Prior: 1.0% | Poll: 0.9% | Surprise: 0.30%
CPI MM: 0.3% | Prior: -0.7% | Poll: -0.1% | Surprise: 0.40%

Professional Market Commentary

The professional tape treated this as a genuine headline reflation shock, but not a clean demand-recovery print. NBS reported CPI at 1.2% y/y and 0.3% m/m, while PPI rose 2.8% y/y and 1.7% m/m; the official explanation emphasized international crude, holiday travel demand, fast-rising commodity prices, selected domestic-demand pockets, and better market-competition order.

Reuters and institutional commentary described PPI as the highest since July 2022 and above poll, with consumer inflation also accelerating. The main caution was that the impulse was narrow, externally driven and not yet a broad reflationary cycle.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is the highest-information EM release of the early-week session because it separates headline reflation from domestic-demand confirmation.

Key signals:

PPI is the primary signal: 2.8% y/y and 1.7% m/m is a large upstream impulse.
The production-goods split dominates the consumer-goods split: means-of-production prices were up strongly, while consumer-goods PPI remained negative.
Mining, oil/gas, non-ferrous metals and chemical-linked categories drove the acceleration.
CPI firmed, but the composition is not broad consumer overheating: food prices fell, pork was weak, and the service impulse was partly holiday/travel-linked.
Core CPI at 1.2% y/y is firmer, but not enough to prove a self-sustaining demand-pull regime.

The internal hierarchy is clear: upstream commodity shock first, energy / travel pass-through second, domestic-demand reflation third and still unproven. This is not a normal “China reflation is back” print. It is a margin-pressure and policy-box print: factory-gate prices are moving before household demand has repaired.

State transition: false dawn — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: China had already been improving through exports and parts of the factory cycle, but the prior EM tape treated that improvement as uneven, partly stockpiling-driven, and not a clean final-demand acceleration. This release confirms the inflation leg of that prior warning rather than validating a healthy domestic reflation story. China remains a stronger nominal-growth headline with weak demand quality underneath.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the release narrows the PBoC easing window without giving Beijing a clean growth victory.

Rates / FX implication:

CNH does not get a clean reflation-positive read because the price impulse is cost-led.
Broad easing becomes harder to justify if PPI is rising sharply, but weak consumer-goods PPI and food deflation still argue against policy tightening.
China beta should be differentiated: upstream / commodity-linked nominal sectors benefit optically; consumer / margin-sensitive sectors face pressure.

Next verification test: China credit aggregates. If TSF, new yuan loans and M2 confirm stronger credit transmission, the false-dawn label can move toward stabilization. If credit disappoints while PPI stays hot, China becomes the clearest EM “wrong reflation” case.

TUESDAY 12 MAY 2026

India — CPI Inflation YY (Apr)
Release Date: 12 May 2026 | Local Time: 12:30
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

CPI Inflation YY: 3.48% | Prior: 3.40% | Poll: 3.80% | Surprise: -0.320%

Professional Market Commentary

The tape framed India CPI as a benign headline miss with a less benign forward skew. MoSPI reported April CPI at 3.48% y/y, with rural inflation above urban inflation and food inflation rising. The official release also showed personal care / jewellery inflation as an outlier, transport inflation nearly flat, and several food items moving sharply in opposite directions.

Post-print commentary emphasized that retail fuel prices had not yet fully reflected the crude shock, leaving fuel repricing and monsoon conditions as key monitorables. Named-economist commentary from the CPI tape kept the RBI in wait-and-see mode, but flagged that rate-hike risk could build later if imported inflation passed through.

Comment — Economist Layer

The mechanical surprise is dovish, but the composition is not fully benign.

Key signals:

Headline CPI undershot poll by 32bp and remains below the RBI’s 4% target midpoint.
Food inflation rose, with rural food inflation above urban.
Transport inflation was effectively flat, which is the key “masked pass-through” element.
Precious metals and personal-care components distort the headline basket upward but do not represent broad domestic-demand overheating.
The imported-inflation channel is present but delayed, not yet fully visible in retail prices.

The main analytical point is timing. The data still argue against an immediate RBI hawkish response, but the forward risk is asymmetric because fuel, fertilizer, logistics and food costs can enter with a lag. This keeps India out of a clean disinflation bucket even though the print missed consensus.

State transition: continuation — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: India had previously been one of the stronger EM domestic-demand stories, with services strength and still-contained inflation supporting a relatively high-quality macro mix. April CPI preserves that advantage mechanically, but the pass-through risk means the earlier “growth with contained prices” setup is becoming more conditional. India remains resilient, but no longer inflation-risk free.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: this does not justify near-term RBI tightening, but it closes any residual easing comfort.

Rates / FX implication:

INR and front-end rates should not treat the headline downside surprise as a durable dovish signal unless fuel pass-through stays suppressed.
RBI can look through one supply shock, but repeated energy / food pass-through would shift the reaction function toward longer pause and eventual hike discussion.
India’s policy trade remains better than Brazil or Turkey, but the direction of travel is less benign than the headline miss suggests.

Next verification test: May CPI and WPI. A WPI acceleration followed by transport CPI pass-through would move the state transition toward deterioration.

Food, chemicals and electrical machinery explain the March improvement.
BER / Absa PMI strength matters, but the front-loading caveat means the survey may be borrowing demand from future months.

The release is therefore a local stabilization event, not a regime break. It is consistent with better near-term operating momentum, but still vulnerable to energy costs, supply disruption and weak credit transmission.

State transition: stabilization — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: South Africa had already moved away from outright weakness, but the prior EM sequence kept the country in a mixed bucket because better activity signals were offset by weak credit and rising pipeline inflation. Brazil — IPCA Inflation Index MM / YY (Apr)

Importance: ****

Reuters Data

IPCA Inflation Index MM: 0.67% | Prior: 0.88% | Poll: 0.69% | Surprise: -0.020%
IPCA Inflation Index YY: 4.39% | Prior: 4.14% | Poll: 4.40% | Surprise: -0.010%

Professional Market Commentary

The tape treated the small downside monthly surprise as misleading. IBGE reported IPCA at 0.67% m/m, below March’s 0.88%, but the 12-month rate rose to 4.39% from 4.14%; food and beverages and health / personal care together accounted for most of the monthly result.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a hawkish inflation-quality print despite the small downside surprise.

Key signals:

The monthly print decelerated, but the annual rate rose 25bp.
The 12-month rate is now only 11bp below the upper bound of the inflation target range.
Food and health dominated the monthly result.
Transportation slowed sharply, but that looks partly like timing rather than a durable inflation offset.
Gasoline rose and diesel pressure remained relevant.
The base effect matters: April 2025 was low, so replacing that with 0.67% mechanically lifts the y/y rate.

The correct hierarchy is not “monthly beat = dovish.” It is: annual inflation moving toward the ceiling, food / health breadth, fuel pass-through still incomplete, and services/core rigidity as the policy constraint. Brazil is not in an inflation crisis, but the release weakens the case for faster easing.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil entered the week with better activity and external support, but the prior EM tape had already warned that producer prices, freight, fuel and services were narrowing BCB policy room. April IPCA confirms that the inflation constraint is moving into the consumer tape even as the headline monthly number slowed. Brazil remains better externally cushioned than fragile EM peers, but its easing cycle is increasingly inflation-capped.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: the release closes the door on an acceleration of Copom cuts.

Rates / FX implication:

DI dovishness based on the monthly downside surprise is fragile.
BRL can still be supported by carry and external accounts, but the inflation mix is no longer cleanly supportive for easing.
Copom can continue gradual cuts only with hawkish calibration; a faster path requires clear evidence that fuel and services are re-anchoring.

Next verification test: May IPCA and services-core momentum. A May print below 0.5% with services cooling would stabilize the path. A fuel / services pass-through would move Brazil into a more explicit policy-constraint deterioration.

Professional Market Commentary

The release is best treated as a USDA WASDE commodity block rather than a Brazil domestic macro release. Reuters routes the series through Brazil RICs, but the underlying publication is USDA WAOB’s May WASDE, covering Brazil-specific soybean and corn production lines inside the global crop balance.

The professional commodity tape frames the report as a “grain divide”: Brazil remains a major supply anchor in soybeans and corn, while the global corn and wheat balances tighten more visibly into 2026/27. USDA’s official tables show Brazil soybean production at 180.00 MMT for 2025/26 and 186.00 MMT for 2026/27, while Brazil corn production is 135.00 MMT for 2025/26 and 139.00 MMT for 2026/27.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a commodity-terms-of-trade and food-inflation transmission block, not a domestic demand block.

Key signals:

Brazil soybean supply leadership is extended: USDA’s first 2026/27 forecast lifts Brazil soy output to 186.00 MMT.
Brazil 2025/26 soy production is 180.00 MMT, broadly in line with the Reuters poll.
Brazil 2025/26 corn is 135.00 MMT, above the Reuters poll, while the first 2026/27 Brazil corn forecast is 139.00 MMT.
The more macro-relevant global signal is not soy scarcity; it is the split between Brazil-led soybean abundance and tighter forward corn / wheat balances.
The crop mix is therefore disinflationary at the soybean-margin level, but not a generalized EM food-disinflation signal.

Verification note: the official WASDE table did not support the scout’s “record-on-record soybean stocks” framing. The usable signal is Brazil production strength plus the corn/wheat divergence, not a record global soybean-stock build.

State transition: continuation — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil had already been treated as a relatively better external-cushion EM, but with inflation and fiscal risks narrowing the policy space. The WASDE block reinforces the external cushion through agriculture supply leadership, while failing to offset the domestic services/fuel inflation constraint. Brazil remains externally supported but domestically policy-constrained.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: marginally supportive for Brazil external accounts, not enough to change the Copom read.

Rates / FX implication:

BRL gets a modest agriculture-export cushion from Brazil’s crop leadership.
That cushion is not equivalent to a dovish inflation impulse because the domestic IPCA / services / fuel channel remains binding.
Food-importing EMs remain exposed to the wheat/corn side of the WASDE balance, especially if summer weather deteriorates.

Next verification test: June–August Northern Hemisphere weather and Brazil export pricing. If corn yield risks intensify while wheat remains tight, the food-inflation channel shifts from crop-specific to broader EM food-import pressure.

WEDNESDAY 13 MAY 2026

Turkey — Current Account Balance (Mar)
Release Date: 13 May 2026 | Local Time: 09:00
Importance: ****

Reuters Data

Current Account Balance: -9.672B | Prior: -7.501B | Poll: -9.625B | Surprise: -0.047B

Professional Market Commentary

The professional tape framed the release as confirmation that Turkey’s external-defence regime is deteriorating again. CBRT reported a March current-account deficit of USD 9.672bn, with the current account excluding gold and energy still in deficit, goods trade the core drag, and the annualized current-account deficit widening materially.

Open wire coverage emphasized that the March deficit was the widest monthly shortfall since January 2023, while also highlighting portfolio outflows and reserve pressure. The key point was not the small miss versus poll; it was the level of the external deficit and the financing quality around it.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is the clearest external-account deterioration print in the EM tape so far.

Key signals:

The deficit is almost exactly in line with Reuters poll, so the surprise is not the market event.
The level is the event: USD 9.672bn is a very large monthly deficit.
The ex-gold-and-energy deficit remains negative, which means the pressure is not only a simple oil/gold story.
Goods are the main drag, while services still provide a partial buffer.
Financing quality deteriorated at the same time: portfolio outflows and reserve drawdown make the current-account deterioration more macro-relevant.

The hierarchy is external balance first, financing mix second, reserve credibility third. Turkey is not merely importing an energy shock; it is absorbing it through a balance-of-payments structure that requires continued confidence, reserves, and high effective rates.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Turkey had already shifted from a narrow stabilization story to an external-fragility regime, with weak trade, falling reserves and broad labor slack undermining the headline adjustment. March current account confirms that trajectory and makes the external constraint the dominant Turkey signal. The regime is now reserve-defence under current-account stress.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: this reinforces CBRT operational tightening and keeps Turkey in a shadow-hike / external-defence configuration.

Rates / FX implication:

TRY remains dependent on administrative defence, high effective funding and reserve credibility.
The curve cannot treat the in-line poll outcome as benign because the financing mix deteriorated.
CDS and reserve data matter more than the current-account surprise magnitude from here.

Next verification test: weekly gross/net FX reserves and April trade. A reserve rebound plus narrower trade gap would stabilize the read; another reserve draw with a wide trade deficit would push the regime further into deterioration.

THURSDAY 14 MAY 2026

India — WPI Inflation YY (Apr)
Release Date: 14 May 2026 | Local Time: 08:30
Importance: ****

Reuters Data

WPI Inflation YY: 8.30% | Prior: 3.88% | Poll: 4.40% | Surprise: 3.90pp

Professional Market Commentary

The institutional read is no longer “CPI contained, imported inflation theoretical.” The official WPI release shows April wholesale inflation at 8.30% y/y, with a 3.86% m/m jump in the all-commodities index. The Ministry release attributes the positive inflation rate primarily to mineral oils, crude petroleum and natural gas, basic metals, other manufacturing and non-food articles; fuel and power rose sharply m/m, manufactured products rose, and 21 of 22 manufactured-product groups recorded m/m price increases.

The tape implication is straightforward: the pass-through that was absent from CPI is visible at the wholesale level. The official detail shows crude petroleum inflation close to 90% y/y, crude petroleum and natural gas above 60% y/y, fuel and power above 20% y/y, and petrol / diesel inflation accelerating sharply.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is the cleanest supply-side shock measurement in the EM tape.

Key signals:

The surprise is large enough to change the India policy read.
The WPI-CPI wedge is now the signal: April CPI stayed below 4%, but WPI has moved to 8.30%.
Fuel and power is the transmission channel, not a residual category.
Manufactured-price breadth matters more than the headline energy spike because it shows cost pressure moving into the production chain.
Electricity m/m weakness does not neutralize the signal because mineral oils, petrol, diesel and crude are doing the heavy lifting.

The prior India CPI block was a benign headline with conditional pass-through risk. WPI converts that risk into a measured pipeline shock. It does not automatically mean immediate RBI tightening, because retail fuel pass-through can still be absorbed fiscally or delayed administratively, but it makes the medium-term rate path less benign.

State transition: deterioration — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: India had been one of the higher-quality EM growth stories, with strong services activity and inflation still close to target. The April CPI release preserved that narrative mechanically, but WPI now shows that the wholesale pipeline has turned materially less benign. India remains a resilient domestic-demand economy, but the policy cushion is now visibly thinner.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: October hike risk is no longer only a scenario; it now has a hard pipeline-inflation data point behind it.

Rates / FX implication:

INR is more vulnerable because subsidy-suppressed CPI now carries a fiscal-cost shadow.
G-sec / OIS pricing should treat the CPI miss as stale information unless May CPI confirms non-pass-through.
RBI can still wait, but the burden of proof shifts: the next CPI and WPI prints must show that this is a reversible energy shock, not a broader cost-push regime.

Next verification test: May CPI fuel / transport and May WPI. If crude-related WPI pressure collapses after a Hormuz de-escalation, this can reverse. If retail transport and manufactured CPI pick up, India moves firmly into policy-constrained deterioration.

Brazil — Service Sector Growth MM (Mar)
Release Date: 15 May 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

Service Sector Growth MM: -1.2% | Prior: 0.1% | Revised: 0.0% | Poll: -0.1% | Surprise: -1.10pp

Professional Market Commentary

This is the most important texture change in the Brazil sequence. IBGE reported that services volume fell 1.2% m/m in March after stability in February, leaving the sector below its October 2025 peak. The decline was broad across all five investigated activities, led by transport, with professional / administrative services, information and communication, other services, and services to families all falling. On a y/y basis, services were still positive, preserving a more mixed rather than outright recessionary read.

Comment — Economist Layer

This print complicates, rather than cancels, the post-IPCA hawkish Brazil read.

Key signals:

The monthly services-volume shock is large relative to poll.
The decline is broad, not a single-sector accident.
Transport is the main drag, but all five surveyed activities fell.
The y/y trend remains positive, so this is not yet an outright services recession signal.
The key cross-print divergence is services prices versus services volumes: services inflation was still sticky in the IPCA tape, while services activity now contracts.

The Brazil macro signal becomes more nuanced. IPCA and retail argued that demand was too firm and inflation too sticky for faster Copom easing. PMS now says the services-volume side is weakening. That does not reopen an easy dovish path because sticky services prices are still the policy problem, but it weakens the simple “positive output gap is closing everywhere” interpretation.

State transition: deterioration — services-specific, conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Brazil had entered the week as externally cushioned but inflation-constrained, with strong retail and sticky services inflation reducing room for faster BCB easing. The March services-volume drop introduces a weaker activity leg inside that story. Brazil remains policy-constrained, but the constraint is now stagflationary rather than simply demand-hot.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: Copom calibration becomes harder, not easier.

Rates / FX implication:

BRL read is mildly negative at the margin because the activity side is less clean.
DI receivers get some support from weaker volume, but services-price rigidity still caps faster easing.
Brazil moves from “growth resilient, inflation-capped easing” toward “sticky prices with uneven activity.”

Next verification test: April PMS and May IPCA services. If services volumes rebound and services prices stay sticky, the hawkish-output-gap read returns. If services volumes contract again while prices remain sticky, Brazil becomes the clearest LatAm stagflationary sub-case.

Poland — Current Account (Mar)
Release Date: 15 May 2026 | Local Time: 14:00
Importance: **

Reuters Data

Current Account: -234M | Prior: -990M | Revised: -1,034M | Poll: -1,215M | Surprise: 981M

Professional Market Commentary

The current-account print is the main 15 May pushback against a one-way Poland / Hormuz deterioration story. ING reported a March current-account deficit of €234mn, better than consensus and February, with the rolling 12-month deficit improving. The improvement came from a narrower goods deficit, stronger exports, a still-large services surplus, and lower secondary-income drag, while primary-income outflows remained large.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is an external-account stabilization print, but not a full reversal of the Poland inflation constraint.

Key signals:

The deficit was much narrower than poll.
The goods deficit improved materially.
Services surplus remains Poland’s external stabilizer.
Exports rose faster than imports.
ING still expects the oil shock to widen the deficit later in the year if energy prices remain elevated.

The release offsets the external-balance part of the Hormuz pressure narrative, but not the CPI part. That distinction matters: Poland is not Turkey. It is not in reserve-defence mode, and the current account remains manageable. But the NBP reaction function is still dominated more by inflation / core / energy than by current-account stress.

State transition: stabilization — conditional.

Context from prior regional live file: Poland had been a resilient CEE economy with some external and energy sensitivity, but not an external-financing stress case. March current account confirms that distinction and partially offsets the downside from Q1 GDP softness. Poland’s constraint remains inflation and rates, not balance-of-payments fragility.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Print reaction function: PLN supportive, POLGB short-end neutral.

Rates / FX implication:

PLN gets support because the external-account surprise pushes back against a simplistic energy-import stress story.
NBP policy pricing should not turn dovish on this print because CPI and core inflation remain the nearer-term constraints.
The Poland trade is now mixed: external stabilization versus inflation confirmation.

Next verification test: April current account and May CPI. A second current-account improvement would reduce external-risk premium; CPI/core reacceleration would keep NBP pinned despite better external data.

SIGNAL TENSION CHECK

Main contradiction: EM still shows the stagflationary fingerprint, but the week is not a one-way deterioration story. India WPI and China credit are the cleanest deterioration signals, while Korea exports and Poland current account provide meaningful offsets.

Why it matters: The same global shock is producing export winners, inflation-constrained central banks, reserve-defence cases, and activity losers.

Implication: EM beta should be traded through country-specific constraint sets: India pipeline inflation, China policy box, Brazil rates complexity, Turkey reserve defence, Korea AI-export resilience, Poland inflation/external split, Mexico activity weakness, and South Africa commodity composition.

3 KEY RELEASES TO DIG INTO

India WPI Inflation YY (14 May 2026)
Why it matters: The clearest quantified wholesale-input shock in the EM tape. It hardens the RBI reaction-function risk even though CPI and labor remain mechanically contained.
China Money & Credit Aggregates (14 May 2026)
Why it matters: Confirms the domestic-demand failure behind the earlier China false-dawn inflation print. Prices up and credit down is the cleanest China policy-box deterioration signal.
Brazil Service Sector Growth MM (15 May 2026)
Why it matters: The most underpriced analytical signal in the final session. Services volumes contracted sharply while services inflation remains sticky, complicating the post-IPCA / post-retail Copom read and turning Brazil from simple hawkish resilience into a more stagflationary calibration problem.

<<EM_WEEK_BEGIN>>
DATA WINDOW: 4 May 2026 to 9 May 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM growth broadened on the surface, with North Asia tech PMIs, India services, Brazil activity/trade and China exports all improving, but the quality of the signal was uneven: a large share of the strength came from AI concentration, commodity windfall, precautionary ordering and front-loading rather than clean final-demand acceleration. Labor evidence was secondary and mostly survey-based, with India and Brazil services still constructive, but Mexico and Turkey weak.

The dominant weekly regime was therefore not clean reflation. Inflation pressure broadened through Turkey CPI, Korea CPI, Taiwan CPI, Brazil IGP-DI, PMI input costs and freight/energy channels, while financial-stability stress was clearest in Turkey reserves. Policy room narrowed across the region: Banxico formalized an end-cycle cut, NBP stayed on hawkish hold, CBRT credibility was re-tested, and Brazil’s better activity/external cushion came with rising producer-price risk. EM ended the week in false-dawn / stabilization-conditional mode: growth stronger, policy cushion thinner.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: +
Supporting evidence:
Growth breadth improved through Korea and Taiwan manufacturing PMIs, India services at 58.8, Brazil services/composite back above 50, Brazil IP beating expectations, Brazil’s large April trade surplus, and China exports rebounding to 14.1% y/y. The signal is positive but not clean: Taiwan trade missed sharply versus expectations, South Africa and Brazil PMIs carried front-loading / cost caveats, and China export strength partly reflected stockpiling.

Labor: ~
Supporting evidence:
The week did not deliver a decisive hard labor signal. Survey evidence was mixed: India services and Brazil services pointed to ongoing activity and jobs support, South Africa PMI showed hiring improvement, while Turkey manufacturing cut staffing and Mexico manufacturing deterioration continued. Labor therefore remains a secondary, unresolved signal rather than the driver of the EM regime.

Inflation: -
Supporting evidence:
Inflation pressure broadened materially. Turkey CPI surprised sharply higher at 4.18% m/m, Korea CPI rose to 2.6% y/y, Taiwan CPI accelerated to 1.74%, Brazil IGP-DI more than doubled to 2.41%, and multiple PMIs flagged input-cost, freight, fuel and supplier-delay pressure. Mexico CPI and PPI softened, and Brazil IPC-Fipe eased, but those offsets did not neutralize the broader producer/imported-cost impulse.

Financial Conditions: -
Supporting evidence:
Turkey was the clearest stress point, with gross FX reserves falling sharply after the CPI shock and weak PMI, making stable-lira disinflation visibly more expensive. Brazil’s trade surplus and carry supported BRL, South Africa reserves were stable, and CNH/TWD had some growth support, but the regional financial-conditions mix deteriorated because reserve credibility, higher input costs and reduced easing optionality became more binding.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
Policy flexibility narrowed across the region. CBRT moved deeper into defensive-hold / hike-risk territory after CPI, weak PMI and reserve drawdown; Banxico cut but with a 3–2 vote and end-cycle guidance; NBP held as stronger domestic data and inflation risk pushed out easing; Brazil’s activity/external improvement was offset by producer-price acceleration; Korea’s CPI/PMI mix removed easing premium and raised hike discussion risk.

C. FULL RELEASE ARCHIVE

MONDAY 4 MAY 2026
South Korea — S&P Global Manufacturing PMI (Apr)
Release Date: 4 May 2026 | Local Time: 02:30
Importance: ***

Reuters Data

S&P Global Mfg PMI: 53.6 | Prior: 52.6

Professional Market Commentary

The professional tape treated the Korean PMI as a strong activity print with an inflationary caveat. The PMI rose to 53.6, the strongest since February 2022, with Reuters and S&P framing the print as semiconductor-led resilience but also noting supply disruption, raw-material stress and conflict-related cost pressure.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is not a pure final-demand acceleration print. It is an export/semi-cycle print, reinforced by some inventory protection and supply-chain hedging.
Key signals:

headline activity strengthened from an already expansionary March base

output and new orders improved

semiconductor demand remains the structural support

input-cost pressure and delivery delays make the release simultaneously a growth and inflation signal

the PMI headline risks overstating underlying demand because precautionary stockbuilding is part of the channel

The hierarchy is therefore: manufacturing resilience first, inflation shock second, artificial strength third. Korea remains one of the cleaner EM beneficiaries of the AI / semiconductor cycle, but April adds a less benign cost-push layer.
State transition: continuation reinforced with hawkish cost drift.
Context from prior regional live file: The prior EM sequence had already framed Korea as an export- and semiconductor-led growth outperformer after the Q1 GDP upside surprise. April PMI reinforces that North Asia tech-resilience bucket, but adds a stronger cost-push and inventory-front-loading overlay. The regime is still resilient growth, but no longer benign for policy.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

KRW and Korea rates should treat this as two-sided: supportive for growth and exports, but not supportive for an easing narrative. The front end remains more sensitive to CPI, oil and BoK communication than to the headline PMI alone. The tactical risk is that markets overpay for the PMI level and underprice the input-cost shock embedded in the same survey.

The next decisive test is whether national inflation confirms the São Paulo IPC-Fipe deceleration or the PMI cost/charge acceleration.
