Taiwan now confirms the same regional impulse in cleaner form: AI-led external demand remains strong enough that policy does not need to ease, but the energy shock has made the inflation side less one-way benign.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

For TWD and Taiwan rates, this is modestly hawkish by implication, not by action. The base case remains a prolonged hold, but the distribution is no longer symmetrical: another growth upgrade or a sustained oil shock would push market pricing toward a tightening conversation faster than toward renewed easing. Cross-regionally, Taiwan now sits at the opposite end of EM from Turkey: one is dealing with growth overperformance plus inflation optionality, the other with external-buffer defense.

This is still a benign pipeline inflation print. The annual rate is less negative, but that is a normalization from very soft producer-price conditions, not a renewed inflation scare. The larger message is that Poland entered the energy-shock phase with producer prices still offering disinflationary cushion. That cushion may now erode, but it has not vanished yet.

This keeps Poland on the benign side of the EM inflation dispersion, though less cleanly than before the oil shock. The strategic question is now how quickly higher imported energy costs feed through and whether that is enough to delay, rather than cancel, future easing.

The right read is that Turkey is using reserves as a geopolitical shock absorber. HF Take — Strategist Layer

This is the most acute financial-stability signal in the week. For TRY and Turkish front-end pricing, the key variable is now duration of external stress, not domestic cyclical nuance. If reserve loss continues at anything close to this pace, the market will keep questioning whether the CBRT can defend the lira without either tighter liquidity for longer or a harder policy reset.

For CNH rates and China-sensitive cyclicals, the takeaway is that the easing cycle is paused rather than reversed. SIGNAL TENSION CHECK

Main contradiction: Backward-looking February and January data still show stabilization or outright improvement in several EM pockets, while forward-looking policy space has narrowed because higher energy prices and geopolitical stress are tightening inflation and external-financing constraints.

Why it matters: Good domestic data are no longer translating one-for-one into easier policy expectations.

Implication: Country selection matters more than broad EM directional narratives.

<<EM_WEEK_BEGIN>>
DATA WINDOW: 9 Mar 2026 to 17 Mar 2026

A. EM WEEK — MACRO SYNTHESIS

EM finished the week in a clear dispersion regime. China improved on nominal tone through firmer CPI/PPI breadth, import-led trade strength, and supportive TSF/M2, but the financing mix still pointed to policy- and government-led support rather than a self-sustaining private-demand recovery. Brazil remained mixed but resilient, with retail and services recovering and IPCA decelerating enough to preserve the easing case without removing debate over pace. South Africa delivered the cleanest positive macro cluster of the week through better GDP, a swing back to current-account surplus, and firmer mining/manufacturing. Against that, Mexico moved more clearly into a stagflationary bind as inflation re-tightened while industrial output deteriorated sharply, and Turkey suffered the week’s most acute deterioration through reserve loss, FX defense, and effective interruption of the easing cycle.

The weekly policy and inflation message was therefore not a broad EM easing green light. Poland confirmed a benign disinflation regime, Brazil kept easing support alive but with monthly frictions, India stayed contained but more oil-sensitive, Mexico became more inflation-constrained again, Korea stayed fragile rather than regime-improved, and Turkey shifted back toward external-fragility management. The resulting EM macro regime is selective domestic resilience under tighter external and oil-shock constraints, with country selection more important than any broad EM beta call.

B. EM MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Growth: ~
Supporting evidence:
China trade was growth-supportive in composition because the smaller surplus reflected stronger imports rather than export weakness, and Brazil retail plus services confirmed that domestic demand was not collapsing. South Africa also improved through firmer GDP, current account, mining, and manufacturing. But Korea’s GDP revision only marginally softened an underlying contractionary Q4, Turkey industry remained weak despite a slight annual improvement, and Mexico industrial output missed sharply on both monthly and yearly measures. The weekly EM growth signal was therefore positive in pockets, but not broad enough to call a clean regional upswing.

Labor: ~
Supporting evidence:
The supplied live file did not materially develop a broad labor signal for EM this week. The archive was dominated by inflation, activity, credit, and external-balance releases rather than employment or wage data. That leaves the labor bucket unresolved rather than positive or negative.

Inflation: ~
Supporting evidence:
China CPI/PPI weakened the deep-deflation narrative, Brazil IPCA decelerated meaningfully on the yearly measure while still showing monthly friction, and Poland confirmed a benign disinflation path. But Mexico headline CPI moved back above Banxico’s 4% upper tolerance threshold with services still sticky, and India CPI printed modestly above expectations with oil pass-through risk still important. The regional inflation signal therefore improved in some places but re-tightened in others, leaving the overall picture mixed rather than cleanly easing-supportive.

Financial Conditions: -
Supporting evidence:
Turkey dominated this bucket. The reserve drawdown, policy hold, and tighter liquidity conditions made the weekly read clearly more defensive and signaled renewed external-financing stress. Korea’s growth backdrop also remained constrained by won weakness and imported-inflation risk as described in the archived analysis, while elsewhere the oil backdrop repeatedly capped confidence in easier conditions. Financial conditions were therefore not uniformly worse across EM, but the week’s marginal signal was negative because the clearest stress event came through Turkey’s reserve and FX channel.

Policy Constraint: -
Supporting evidence:
Brazil preserved the case for COPOM easing, but not with enough cleanliness to settle the 25bp versus 50bp debate. India’s CPI and oil sensitivity favored RBI pause rather than renewed easing, Mexico’s inflation threshold breach kept Banxico in a cautious-slow easing posture despite weaker growth, and Turkey moved most clearly in the wrong direction as reserve stress effectively interrupted the easing cycle. Poland’s current inflation backdrop remained benign, but even there the forward debate shifted toward energy risk. The weekly policy message was therefore that easing remained possible in parts of EM, but the aggregate constraint set tightened rather than loosened.

The important distinction is CPI breadth versus still-negative PPI. HF Take — Strategist Layer

This release raises the chance that China stops acting as a clean global disinflation offset. For the global overlay, that matters because it lands against weak Europe and ahead of key US inflation data. It is supportive of a selective reflation narrative in EM, but not yet a full regime turn.

MEXICO — CPI / Core CPI / PPI (Feb)

Release Date: 9 Mar 2026 | Local Time: —

Reuters Data

CPI YY: 4.02% | Prior: 3.79% | Poll: ~3.94% | Surprise: +0.08pp
CPI MM: 0.50% | Prior: 0.38%
Core CPI YY: ~4.52% | Prior: 4.52% | Poll: ~4.50% | Surprise: ~0.00%

Professional Market Commentary

Institutional commentary treated the release as a meaningful inflation re-acceleration rather than a clean inflation scare. The key tape focus was that headline CPI moved back above Banxico’s 4% upper tolerance threshold, mainly on food and vegetable prices, while services inflation remained sticky enough to keep Banxico cautious. Commentary also emphasized that oil and tariff pass-through risks now shift attention toward March-April inflation prints rather than allowing a clean easing narrative.

Comment — Economist Layer

The main signal is not just the threshold breach itself, but the composition. Headline inflation moved above 4%, but the proximate driver appears to be volatile food and vegetable prices rather than a broad-based demand reacceleration. That limits how hawkish the print should be read. The more important structural signal is services inflation at 4.45%, because that is the part of the basket Banxico is less able to dismiss as temporary. So the correct read is: inflation has become more constraining again, even if the immediate driver is partly non-core.

There is also an information gap on PPI. No confirmed February PPI print was retrieved in the provided tape, so this block should not treat producer prices as a confirmed macro signal.

State transition: deterioration

Context from prior regional live file:
The prior Mexico sequence had been moving along a cautious-disinflation path, with Banxico already in a restrained easing posture rather than an aggressive one. February weakens that benign trajectory. The first breach of the 4% ceiling in this cycle is a meaningful tightening of the inflation constraint, especially because it arrives alongside already-softening industrial activity.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

For Banxico, this keeps easing alive only in a cautious, slow form. The threshold breach does not force a hawkish reversal on its own, but it removes residual dovish urgency and makes the next oil-sensitive inflation prints much more important. For markets, Mexico now looks more clearly stuck in a stagflationary bind: weaker growth momentum, but inflation not soft enough to justify fast cuts.

CHINA — Exports / Imports / Trade Balance (Feb)

Release Date: 10 Mar 2026 | Local Time: —

Reuters Data

Exports YoY: +39.6% | Prior: +9.8% | Poll: +7.1% | Surprise: +32.50%
Imports YoY: +13.8% | Prior: +25.6% | Poll: +6.3% | Surprise: +7.50%
Trade Balance USD: 90.98B | Prior: 122.64B | Poll: 179.60B | Surprise: -88.620B

Professional Market Commentary

Professional commentary focused less on the headline surplus miss and more on the strong import print. The key read was that import strength across commodities, consumer goods, and semiconductors points to broader nominal demand and restocking rather than a narrow export-only story.

Comment — Economist Layer

The composition is the story. A smaller trade surplus caused by stronger imports is a healthier signal than a surplus miss caused by export weakness. That makes this release more relevant for the global growth map than the headline balance alone, especially because it lines up with the firmer China CPI/PPI signal.

Context from prior regional live file:
December trade had already softened the “China demand is dead” narrative, and the broader EM week synthesis had treated China trade plus credit beats as the core EM impulse. February therefore extends and strengthens an existing upswing rather than creating it from scratch, with the stronger-import / smaller-surplus mix adding a healthier domestic-absorption element.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

This release strengthens the case that China is the leading upside impulse within EM this week. In cross-zone terms, it offsets part of Europe’s weakness and prevents the global narrative from collapsing into a one-way slowdown call. The key conditional next step is whether financing data validate the activity pulse.

TURKEY — Industrial Production (Jan)

Release Date: 10 Mar 2026 | Local Time: —

Reuters Data

Industrial Production YY: -1.8% | Prior: -2.1% | Surprise: +0.3pp
Industrial Production MM SA: -2.8% | Prior: +1.2%
Manufacturing YY: -2.5% | Prior: -2.7%
Mining and Quarrying YY: -2.8% | Prior: +2.0%
Electricity / Gas / Steam YY: +5.6% | Prior: +2.4%

Professional Market Commentary

Institutional commentary treated the release as mildly better on the annual rate but still weak in underlying terms. The tape focus was that Turkey’s industrial sector remains under pressure from tight monetary conditions and weak domestic demand, while the monthly drop shows that recovery had not yet taken hold. Commentary also highlighted that production appears to be lagging demand conditions, suggesting some stabilization in orders without a convincing recovery in output.

Comment — Economist Layer

The right read is mixed but still weak. On a year-on-year basis, the contraction moderated slightly, which is directionally better than December. But the seasonally adjusted monthly fall of -2.8% is a sharp reversal and warns against reading the annual improvement as a turning point. Manufacturing remains negative, mining reversed, and only energy-related output looks clearly positive.

That leaves the industrial cycle in a “still contracting, but maybe bottoming unevenly” state rather than recovery. The broad macro implication is that Turkey entered the March reserve/oil shock episode with industry already fragile. That matters because the industrial sector was implicitly relying on gradual monetary relief later in 2026, and that relief is now less secure.

State transition: continuation with marginal improvement

Context from prior regional live file:
The earlier Turkey live sequence had been moving toward slower contraction rather than outright recovery. January IP fits that exact pattern. It marginally improves the annual trajectory, but not enough to change the broader industrial picture. After the March 12 reserve and rate block, this release reads even more weakly in hindsight because the main hoped-for recovery channel — easing financial conditions — has become less certain.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

Standalone, this is a low-conviction market release. But in sequence, it matters because it shows Turkey’s industrial base was not recovering before the external shock hit. That makes the reserve drawdown and rate-cut suspension more consequential for the forward growth path. For assets, the implication is that Turkey’s cyclical recovery remains conditional on renewed room for easing, which now depends more heavily on the oil and FX backdrop.

SOUTH AFRICA — GDP (Q4)

Release Date: 10 Mar 2026 | Local Time: —

Reuters Data

GDP QQ SA: 0.4% | Prior: 0.3% | Poll: 0.3% | Surprise: +0.10pp
GDP YY: 0.8% | Prior: 2.1%
Full-year 2025 GDP: 1.1%

Professional Market Commentary

Institutional commentary treated the release as constructive but not strong enough to justify a full recovery narrative. The tape emphasized that South Africa avoided a more negative outcome and delivered a modest beat, helped by stronger household consumption and services, but also stressed that full-year growth remained weak in per-capita terms and below Treasury expectations. Forward commentary was already heavily conditioned by the oil shock and its implications for inflation, fiscal risk, and the SARB easing path.

Comment — Economist Layer

The quarterly beat is real, but the quality of growth matters. Household consumption was the main support, while finance and services outperformed. Manufacturing remained weak and fixed investment stayed structurally soft. That means the economy is growing, but through a relatively narrow and not especially productivity-enhancing mix. The full-year 1.1% number is better than the prior year, yet still weak in absolute terms and below what would be needed to improve per-capita performance meaningfully.

So this is an improvement print, but it is fragile and below potential. It is best read as “less bad, with some cyclical help,” not “South Africa has entered a durable recovery regime.”

State transition: improvement

Context from prior regional live file:
The prior South Africa sequence had been mixed and not yet sufficient to sustain a strong growth-positive narrative. Q4 GDP improves that picture by showing better household demand and positive quarterly momentum. In retrospect, when paired with the later current account, mining, and manufacturing beats, it becomes part of the strongest South Africa data cluster of the week — though still one made fragile by the oil shock overlay.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

This release is supportive for ZAR and for keeping the SARB easing path alive, because it improves the growth backdrop without yet producing a new inflation problem. But the support is conditional. If the oil shock persists, the benefit of this GDP beat can be quickly overshadowed by higher fuel costs, inflation risk, and reduced room for policy easing.

THURSDAY 12 MAR 2026

TURKEY — Current Account Balance / CBT Weekly Repo Rate / FX Reserves (Jan / Mar / 6 Mar, w/e)

Release Date: 12 Mar 2026 | Local Time: 08:00 / 12:00 / 12:30

Reuters Data

Current Account Balance, Jan: -6.807B | Prior: -7.253B
CBT Weekly Repo Rate, Mar: 37.00% | Prior: 37.00% | Poll: 37.00% | Surprise: 0.000%
O/N Lending Rate, Mar: 40.00% | Prior: 40.00%
O/N Borrowing Rate, Mar: 35.50% | Prior: 35.50%
Late Liquidity Window Rate, Mar: 43.00% | Prior: 43.00%
Gross FX Reserves, 6 Mar w/e: 62.77B | Prior: 73.43B
Net FX Reserves, 6 Mar w/e: 78.78B | Prior: 91.78B

Professional Market Commentary

Institutional commentary overwhelmingly focused on the reserve drawdown rather than the current account improvement or the on-hold policy rate. The dominant tape signal was that the CBRT used reserves aggressively to defend the lira as the Middle East oil shock and broader EM pressure hit Turkey’s external financing channel. Commentary also treated the March hold at 37% alongside tighter liquidity conditions as a de facto interruption of the easing cycle.

Comment — Economist Layer

The current account print is directionally better, but it is not the macro signal that matters in this block. The dominant information is the reserve loss. A modest narrowing in the January external deficit is overwhelmed by the scale of the weekly reserve depletion, which indicates active FX defense and a live external vulnerability problem. The rate hold itself is mechanically unsurprising, but the combination of no cut plus liquidity tightening implies the policy reaction function has turned more defensive.

State transition: deterioration

Context from prior regional live file:
The earlier Turkey sequence had been gradually shifting from extreme stress toward more controlled disinflation and managed depreciation. This release interrupts that stabilization story. The reserve drawdown is effectively a reversal of prior buffer rebuilding and moves the dominant regime signal back toward external fragility.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

For markets, Turkey is again trading through the oil shock → lira pressure → reserve depletion → delayed easing loop. The current account improvement does little to offset that near-term dynamic. The key conditional variable is duration: if oil pressure fades quickly, the reserve shock can remain a contained interruption; if it persists, the cut cycle stays suspended and Turkish assets remain constrained by external financing stress.

INDIA — CPI Inflation (Feb)

Release Date: 12 Mar 2026 | Local Time: 11:30

Reuters Data

CPI Inflation YY, Feb: 3.21% | Prior: 2.75% | Revised: 2.73% | Poll: 3.10% | Surprise: 0.110%

Professional Market Commentary

Professional commentary treated the print as a modest upside surprise but not a hawkish shock. The institutional emphasis was on two points: first, the release supports an RBI pause rather than renewed easing; second, the new CPI methodology complicates clean historical comparison and increases measurement fog just as the oil shock raises forward inflation risk.

Comment — Economist Layer

The signal is less about the small beat itself than about the forward path. At 3.21%, inflation remains well within the tolerance band, but the combination of higher oil sensitivity and RBI’s own projected path toward firmer inflation later in the fiscal year makes further near-term easing difficult to justify. The methodological change also matters: this is still an early print in a new CPI series, so the trend should be interpreted with caution. That reduces confidence in any strong “inflation is solved” inference.

State transition: continuation with mild upside pressure

Context from prior regional live file:
The prior India story was already one of contained inflation with easing space narrowing rather than expanding. February reinforces that structure. It does not create a new inflation problem, but it does close residual room for an early-cut interpretation, especially under an oil shock overlay.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

For India, the read-through is mainly policy-temporal: this print supports an RBI pause rather than opening a new easing window. The market consequence is less about the level of February CPI and more about how March-April prints behave under the new CPI framework if oil stays elevated. That makes the oil pass-through the key conditional macro variable from here.

Comment — Economist Layer

The annual number is the more important macro signal: 3.81% is a meaningful deceleration from 4.44% and keeps inflation inside the tolerance band. The data alone supports cuts beginning, but not necessarily aggressive confidence on pace.

State transition: stabilization with easing support, but not cleanly

Context from prior regional live file:
The prior Brazil sequence was already mixed: softer inflation trend developing, but activity not collapsing and policy still constrained by credibility and inflation expectations. February IPCA fits that same structure. It is good enough to preserve the cut case, but not strong enough to remove the debate over magnitude.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

The release keeps a March COPOM cut as the base case but leaves open a live 25bp versus 50bp debate. For cross-asset interpretation, that means Brazil remains one of the more constructive EM easing stories, but with oil and monthly inflation composition still capping confidence. The print is supportive, though not sufficiently clean to unlock an aggressive repricing of the easing path.

State transition: continuation

Context from prior regional live file:
The prior Poland inflation story had already been one of orderly disinflation and growing room for policy easing. February final does not change that path. HF Take — Strategist Layer

This release has low immediate market value because it confirms what was already known. But it helps preserve the broader interpretation that Poland’s domestic inflation backdrop is not the current problem. The conditional issue is whether the oil shock interrupts what would otherwise have been a more extended easing path later in 2026.

CHINA — Total Social Financing / M2 Money Supply / New Yuan Loans / Outstanding Loan Growth (Feb)

Release Date: 13 Mar 2026 | Local Time: 10:02 / 10:03

Reuters Data

Total Social Financing, Feb: 2,380.0B | Prior: 7,220.0B | Poll: 2,133.0B | Surprise: 247.00B
M2 Money Supply YY, Feb: 9.0% | Prior: 9.0% | Poll: 8.8% | Surprise: 0.20%
New Yuan Loans, Feb: 900.0B | Prior: 4,710.0B | Poll: 979.0B | Surprise: -79.00B
Outstanding Loan Growth, Feb: 6.0% | Prior: 6.1% | Poll: 6.0% | Surprise: 0.00%

Professional Market Commentary

The institutional reading was split rather than uniformly positive or negative. Commentary treated the TSF beat and M2 beat as evidence of supportive liquidity and fiscal-led financing, while the loan miss kept the focus on weak private-sector credit demand. The main narrative was that China’s financing impulse remains government-driven rather than demand-led.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a bifurcated print. The TSF beat is not a straightforward growth-positive signal because the composition points toward government issuance rather than stronger private borrowing appetite. The loan miss is the cleaner private-demand signal and remains weak. M2 resilience is constructive for liquidity conditions, but liquidity is not the same as autonomous credit creation. So the macro message is: policy support is still working through public channels while private credit demand remains impaired.

State transition: no material change in the core regime

Context from prior regional live file:
The prior China sequence had already moved toward “less disinflationary, better nominal tone, but still not a self-sustaining private-demand recovery.” This release fits that same path. It validates the government-led financing story rather than upgrading the macro regime into a clean private-credit reflation phase.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

For markets, this keeps China in a fiscal-support / soft-private-demand configuration. That matters because it preserves some support for EM/global growth without resolving the underlying weakness in domestic private credit transmission. The key conditional implication is that fiscal tools remain the primary macro lever unless later data show stronger household and corporate borrowing.

MEXICO — Industrial Output (Jan)

Release Date: 13 Mar 2026 | Local Time: 13:00

Reuters Data

Industrial Output YY, Jan: -1.1% | Prior: 2.4% | Poll: 1.7% | Surprise: -2.80%
Industrial Output MM, Jan: -1.1% | Prior: 0.2% | Revised: 0.1% | Poll: 0.0% | Surprise: -1.10%

Professional Market Commentary

Institutional commentary read this as one of the most negative surprises in the EM block. The narrative focused on broad-based industrial weakness, the fragility of the late-2025 recovery, and the heavier structural backdrop of weak investment, tariff uncertainty, and USMCA-related caution. The release was framed less as a one-off miss and more as evidence that Mexico’s industrial cycle remains fundamentally constrained.

Comment — Economist Layer

This is a genuinely weak print. Both the yearly and monthly measures miss sharply, and the breadth described in the scout points away from a narrow distortion story. The larger signal is that Mexico’s industrial side remains structurally fragile: weak investment, tariff-related cost pressure, and external-policy uncertainty are all consistent with a softer production base. The data therefore argue against reading prior improvement as a durable turn.

State transition: deterioration

Context from prior regional live file:
The prior Mexico sequence had been cautious rather than optimistic, with softness in the underlying industrial and investment picture already visible beneath occasional firmer prints. January now materially weakens the idea of a sustained rebound and pushes the trajectory back toward structural industrial underperformance.

HF Take — Strategist Layer

For Mexico, the release strengthens the case for further easing in growth terms but does not automatically accelerate Banxico because inflation and external-risk constraints remain active. The more important cross-asset message is that Mexico’s macro problem is becoming more structurally investment- and trade-regime-linked, not just cyclically soft. That raises the relevance of the USMCA review and tariff structure for the medium-term MXN and rates narrative.

SIGNAL TENSION CHECK

Main contradiction: EM domestic resilience improved in Brazil, South Africa, and parts of China, but external/oil-shock constraints tightened sharply for Turkey and kept policy easing paths cautious elsewhere.
Why it matters: The regional story is not a single EM beta call; it is a dispersion regime.
Implication: Country selection matters more than broad EM directional narratives.

3 KEY RELEASES TO DIG INTO

Turkey — Current Account Balance / CBT Weekly Repo Rate / FX Reserves (12 Mar 2026)
Why it matters: The reserve drawdown is the most acute external-vulnerability signal in the EM week. It directly affects the lira, the CBRT reaction function, and the durability of Turkey’s disinflation/easing narrative.

China — Total Social Financing / M2 Money Supply / New Yuan Loans / Outstanding Loan Growth (13 Mar 2026)
Why it matters: The split between TSF strength and weak loan demand is central for judging whether China’s support is evolving into genuine private-sector recovery or staying government-led. That distinction matters for the broader EM and global growth impulse.

Mexico — Industrial Output (13 Mar 2026)
Why it matters: The scale of the miss suggests Mexico’s industrial weakness is structural rather than incidental. It has implications for Banxico, investment expectations, and the 2026 USMCA/tariff macro regime.

MACRO SIGNAL SCOREBOARD

Demand: ~ Mixed
Supporting releases: India GDP and PMIs stayed very strong; Taiwan export orders and industrial output remained exceptionally strong and clearly tech-led; Brazil services/composite PMI improved while GDP/consumption stayed soft; China official PMI remained weak even as private PMIs rebounded; Poland industry and PMI stayed weak; Turkey GDP slowed with investment under pressure.
Interpretation: EM demand remains bifurcated. Tech/export-led Asia and India look strong, while parts of CEEMEA and official China manufacturing remain softer.

Labor: ~ Mixed / Softening in spots
Supporting releases: India unemployment rose mainly on the urban side; Poland unemployment rose but the tape suggests seasonality mattered; Turkey labour indicators worsened but were not clearly a full structural break; Taiwan labour stayed stable.
Interpretation: Labour softening exists, but it is uneven and in several cases partly seasonal or sector-specific.

Inflation: ~ Mixed
Supporting releases: India WPI accelerated on primary articles more than broad core pressure; Brazil IPCA-15 was food-led while IGP gauges stayed deflationary; South Africa CPI stayed low but food firmed and PPI softened; Korea CPI stayed benign with food up and energy down; Taiwan CPI rose partly on Lunar New Year effects; Turkey monthly CPI improved but the broader inflation regime remains very high.
Interpretation: EM inflation is still mixed and composition-sensitive. Several pipeline and seasonal effects matter more than the simple headline direction.

Financial Conditions: ~ Mixed / Selective Easing Bias
Supporting releases: China LPR stayed unchanged, signaling policy caution; Poland delivered a cut; Korea inflation near 2% preserves pause space; Turkey reserves remained volatile and NPLs edged higher.
Interpretation: Policy settings remain cautious rather than uniformly dovish. Poland is the clearest easing case; Turkey remains financially fragile; China still looks hesitant on transmission.

DATA QUALITY FLAG
Seasonal distortion risk: Medium
Revision sensitivity: Medium
Signal confidence: Moderate

SIGNAL TENSION CHECK
Strong investment- and tech-led activity in India, Taiwan, and Korea coexists with weak official China manufacturing, soft Poland industry, and fragile Turkey external/labour dynamics.
Implication:
EM should not be treated as one macro bucket. The main tension is between strong Asia tech/export cycles and more fragile domestic-demand or policy-stressed EM economies where reserves, investment, or industrial activity remain under pressure.

MONDAY 03 FEB — RELEASED

TURKEY — CPI (Jan)
• Monthly: 4.84% vs Consensus: 4.32% vs Prior: 0.89%
• Annual: 30.65% vs Consensus: 30.00% vs Prior: 30.89%

PROFESSIONAL COMMENTARY (aggregated from public sources):
→ Trading Economics: "Monthly CPI surged to one-year high of 4.84% from 0.89%, surpassing expectations of 4.32%. Reflects TurkStat's overhaul of inflation methodology - rebasing index, revising basket categories, shifting weights from household surveys to national accounts data."
→ P.A. Turkey Analyst İris Cibre: "Every year basket weights change. General principle: items rising faster than headline gain weight, slower lose weight. Housing weight either stagnated or declined despite rent prices rising 61%. This cannot be explained. If old method used, inflation would have been much higher. What we see now is already the reduced version."
→ Former CBT Chief Economist Prof. Hakan Kara: "New CPI index may measure inflation at higher levels. TurkStat's decision to switch despite that supports institutional credibility. However, Central Bank will revise year-end inflation forecast from 16% to 19%. I keep my own forecast unchanged at 25% — well above official targets."
→ ING Economist (Dec 2025 comment): "We expect 2026 inflation at 22%, risks significantly on upside. December data should encourage CBT to continue rate cuts by 150bp, but continuing inflation risks could keep bank cautious."
→ Central Bank blog (Merkezin Güncesi): "CPI basket now places significantly greater weight on services (+7.4ppt), while energy fell 3.2ppt, core goods 3.0ppt. Upward impact on annual inflation expected ~1ppt."

COMMENT (HF sensitivity):
Dominant signal: Turkey CPI 4.84% MM = HYPERINFLATION RETURN risk. This is NOT "base effect" or "seasonal" — it's a 540% ANNUALIZED monthly rate (4.84% × 12 months = 58%+ annual if sustained). The spike from 0.89% prior month = 5.4X ACCELERATION in ONE MONTH. This is a REGIME BREAK. CRITICAL: Methodology change provides COVER for statistical manipulation. Analysts (Cibre, Kara) explicitly state "if old method used, inflation would be higher" + "housing weight declined despite 61% rent inflation = cannot be explained." This creates CREDIBILITY CRISIS.
Secondary: Annual inflation 30.65% is DOWN from 30.89%, which seems benign, but this is MISLEADING — the monthly acceleration (0.89% → 4.84%) signals future UPWARD trajectory. Forecasters now expecting 22-25% YY inflation for end-2026 (vs CBT official 16% target).
Noise: Base effects from 2025 are helping keep annual number down temporarily, but monthly momentum is the real signal
Reaction-function impact (CBT): This puts CBT in IMPOSSIBLE position: (a) If they hold repo 50.00% (hawkish), inflation still 30%+ = negative real rates, TRY collapses; (b) If they cut rates (as ING suggested pre-data), inflation spirals further. Most likely path: CBT FORCED TO HOLD 50.00% through Q1 2026 minimum, then cuts 100-150bp Q2 if inflation moderates (but unlikely given momentum). Deputy Governor Heath's "credibility crisis" comment (from Mexico Banxico context, but applicable) rings true.
Transmission: TRY in CRISIS ZONE. Reserves falling (see Feb 5 data below) + CPI accelerating + methodology doubts = triple threat. TRY likely tests 40-45 vs USD in Q1 2026 (from current ~35-36) unless: (a) CBT emergency hike (unlikely), (b) FX controls imposed (tail risk), (c) external financing secured (IMF? Gulf states? — both politically difficult). Turkey sovereign CDS likely spikes 200-300bp.
Regime trigger: If monthly CPI >5% for 2-3 consecutive months (March/April 2026), Turkey enters hyperinflation spiral (>50% annual by June). Threshold: CBT repo 50.00% + CPI 35%+ YY by April = crisis.

The CRITICAL shift: inflation target convergence pushed from Q3 2026 → Q2 2027 = ADMISSION that inflation stickier than expected. Secondary: UNANIMOUS vote (no dissent) vs prior 4-1 split votes = Board UNIFIED in pause decision, reducing odds of near-term cut
Noise: Single hold vs hold not informative; need March meeting to confirm if pause = "skip" or "pivot"
Reaction-function impact (Banxico): Forward guidance shift ("timing" vs "reducing") is HAWKISH. This signals: (a) March cut unlikely unless core cooperates (<4.3%), (b) Easing cycle resume May/June if: core inflation moderates, USDMXN stable, Fed holds/cuts. Terminal rate likely 6.50% (from Scotiabank forecast), but timing extended — reach 6.50% by Q3-Q4 2026 (not mid-year as prior expectations).
Transmission: MXN SUPPORTED near-term by pause (carry 7.00% vs Fed 4.50% = 250bp differential maintained). However, MXN vulnerable to: (a) Mexico growth miss (IGAE -0.1% Week 1 data), (b) US tariff threats (Trump trade policy), (c) Banxico eventual resumption of cuts (May/June). MXN range: 17.20-17.80 vs USD near-term, but downside risk to 18.00-18.50 if growth deteriorates or US tariffs imposed.
Regime shift: Banxico has moved from "AGGRESSIVE EASING" (50bp cuts in 2025) → "CAUTIOUS PAUSE" (data-dependent, core inflation watching) → likely "GRADUAL EASING" (25bp cuts Q2-Q3 2026 if conditions allow). This makes MXN less attractive carry trade (cuts coming eventually) but less vulnerable than TRY/BRL (which are in crisis/recession mode).

**TAIWAN:**
- Growth: 12.68% Q4 (highest in 38 years)
- Inflation: 0.69% (MAJOR disinflation despite boom)

- FX: TWD appreciation pressure (fundamentals + US pressure on current account surplus >15% GDP)
- **Regime:** "Disinflation Puzzle" — export boom (AI chips) but domestic weak = K-shaped economy

**KEY INSIGHT:** India > Taiwan in quality because India has DOMESTIC-LED growth (PMI domestic orders strong) while Taiwan is EXPORT-DEPENDENT (11.91ppt of 12.68ppt GDP from net exports). If global AI demand plateaus, Taiwan crashes; India has resilience.

---

**TIER 4 — "CRISIS MODE" (Twin Crises: Inflation + FX Reserves):**

**TURKEY:**
- Growth: Not reported (but prior moderate)
- Inflation: **CPI 4.84% MM (HYPERINFLATION SPIKE) vs 0.89% prior**, annual 30.65%
- Policy: CBT 50.00% (forced to hold despite negative real rates), cuts unlikely until crisis passes
- FX Reserves: **NET 93.36B (REVERSED -4.01B from +6.36B prior week) = CREDIBILITY CRISIS**
- **Regime:** "TWIN CRISIS" — CPI accelerating (4.84% MM = 58%+ annualized if sustained) + reserves collapsing (burning 4B/week to defend TRY) + methodology doubts (statisticians saying "real inflation higher"). This is UNSUSTAINABLE.

**TURKEY CRISIS MECHANICS:**
1. **Inflation shock:** CPI 4.84% MM is 5.4X acceleration from 0.89% prior. If sustained for 2-3 months, annual inflation explodes to 35-40%+ by April.
2. **Reserve burn:** -4.01B in one week = 16B/month annualized = 192B/year. Net reserves 93.36B / monthly burn 16B = 5.8 months runway.
3. **Methodology doubts:** Analysts (Cibre, Kara) flagging basket weight manipulation (housing down despite 61% rent inflation), creating CREDIBILITY CRISIS.
4. **Policy trap:** CBT repo 50.00% vs CPI 30.65% annual (4.84% MM implies higher) = NEGATIVE REAL RATES even at 50% nominal. Hiking to positive real (60-70% repo?) would crash economy; holding 50% lets inflation spiral.
5. **FX pressure:** TRY 35-36 vs USD currently, likely 40-45 by March if reserve burn continues.

**CONTAGION RISK:** Turkey is IDIOSYNCRATIC (Erdogan unorthodox policy, CBT independence compromised), so limited direct contagion to other EM. However, if Turkey enters acute crisis (reserves <85B, TRY >45, IMF forced), could create risk-off sentiment spillover to other frontier EM (Egypt, Pakistan, Argentina). Core EM (India, Taiwan, Korea, Brazil, Mexico) insulated.

"EM divergence extreme — India/Taiwan booming (growth + disinflation); China/Brazil/Mexico stress (growth slowing); Turkey credibility rebuild (reserves +6.36B)"

**UPDATED REGIME (Post-Week 2):**
**"EM POLARIZATION ACCELERATING — India/Taiwan 'Perfect Combo' (growth high + inflation low + policy stable = strongest EM fundamentals); Turkey CRISIS MODE (hyperinflation return CPI 4.84% MM + reserve collapse -4.01B = twin crisis unsustainable); China/Brazil/Mexico dovish pivots CONFIRMED (growth collapsing, easing coming/resumed); Central bank divergence at HISTORICAL MAXIMUM (RBI 'hold forever' vs PBoC 'urgent easing' vs CBT 'trapped')."**

**DOMINANT CROSS-EM NARRATIVE:**
The "GROWTH/INFLATION SCISSORS" identified in Week 1 are now WIDENING into REGIME POLARIZATION:
- **India/Taiwan:** Growth + disinflation = central banks can hold indefinitely = FX/equity strength
- **Turkey:** Hyperinflation + reserve collapse = central bank trapped = FX/equity crisis
- **China/Brazil/Mexico:** Growth collapse + dovish pivots = FX weakening + equity vulnerable to earnings downgrades

This creates **MAXIMUM EM FX DISPERSION** (INR/TWD vs TRY spread widest since 2018 Turkey crisis) and **MAXIMUM ALPHA OPPORTUNITY** in EM equity selection (overweight India/Taiwan tech, underweight Turkey/China consumer, neutral Brazil/Mexico).

**REGIME TRIGGERS (What Would Change This View):**

**BULLISH TRIGGER (EM-wide rally, reduces divergence):**
→ **China MASSIVE stimulus at March NPC:** Fiscal deficit >5% GDP + RRR cut 100bp + property bailout = CNH stabilizes at 7.30, EM risk-on rally
→ **Fed DOVISH PIVOT:** 50bp March cut + "growth concerns" = EM FX broad rally, reduces carry advantage but lifts all boats
→ **Turkey EXTERNAL BAILOUT:** IMF deal or Gulf state financing (Saudi/UAE/Qatar) secures reserves = TRY stabilizes at 38-40, crisis averted

**BEARISH TRIGGER (EM-wide selloff, contagion):**
→ **Turkey ACUTE CRISIS:** Reserves <85B + TRY >50 + capital controls imposed = EM risk-off contagion, even though Turkey idiosyncratic
→ **India INFLATION SHOCK:** Food crisis (monsoon failure, oil spike) → CPI 2.1% → 5.0%+ → RBI forced to hike 50bp = INR crashes, Nifty -15%
→ **Taiwan AI DEMAND PLATEAU:** Nvidia revenue miss + TSMC order cancellations = GDP 12.68% → <2% in single quarter, TWD/TAIEX crash
→ **China HARD LANDING:** Feb + March PMI <48 for 3 consecutive months + IP <4.0% = CNH 7.50+, commodity crash, EM contagion

**NEUTRAL TRIGGER (Status Quo Extends):**
→ **Gradual EM differentiation:** India/Taiwan continue outperforming (India IP 6-7%, Taiwan GDP 6-8% more sustainable), Turkey muddles through (reserve burn slows, TRY 38-42 range), China gradual easing (25bp cuts, modest fiscal) = Current divergence persists through H1 2026
→ **Fed HOLDS March:** No cut, no hike, data-dependent = EM FX stable, carry trades attractive, no major catalyst either direction

---

**WEEK 2 CONCLUSION:**

The key takeaway is that EM is NO LONGER A SINGLE ASSET CLASS — it's now THREE DISTINCT REGIMES:

1. **"QUALITY EM"** (India, Taiwan): Growth + disinflation + policy stability = long conviction
2. **"TRANSITION EM"** (China, Brazil, Mexico, Korea, SA, Poland): Growth slowing, easing coming, tactical trades
3. **"CRISIS EM"** (Turkey): Hyperinflation + reserve collapse = avoid

Investors must differentiate WITHIN EM, not treat as homogenous. The spread between INR (strongest) and TRY (weakest) is now at 2018 levels, creating **MAXIMUM EM ALPHA OPPORTUNITY** for those who can navigate the divergence.

• Actual: 15.00% HOLD vs Consensus: 15.00%

Dominant signal: Hold as expected, but CONTEXT matters — BCB holding at cycle peak (15.00%) while growth softening and inflation cooperating. Minutes/guidance will signal timing of dovish pivot.
Secondary: Brazil entering dovish window — IP contracting, unemployment rising, IPCA inflation falling toward 4.5% target
Noise: Single meeting hold vs hold is not informative; need statement language on "prolonged restrictiveness" vs "data-dependent"
Reaction-function impact (BCB): First cut likely March or May (50bp); terminal rate 11.00-11.50% by end-2026. Easing cycle will be GRADUAL (50bp steps, not 100bp) given inflation still above target.
Transmission: BRL supportive near-term (carry 15% is massive), but vulnerable when cuts begin. Rates 15.00% → 11.00% over 12 months = 400bp easing = BRL weakening pressure. Timing: BRL stable Jan-Feb, weakens Mar onwards.

THURSDAY 30 JAN — RELEASED

TAIWAN — GDP Q4 (preliminary)
• Actual: 12.68% YY vs Consensus: 8.50% vs Prior: 8.20% (Q3)
• Full-year 2025 GDP: 8.63% (15-year high)

PROFESSIONAL COMMENTARY (aggregated from public sources):
→ Taiwan statistics agency: "Q4 growth surpassed forecasts due to unexpectedly robust AI-related demand and absence of US tariffs on semiconductor products" — Chiang Hsin-yi (agency official)
→ ING Economist: "2025 delivered simple message: we were clearly not bullish enough on tech boom. Net exports contributed 11.91ppt of 12.68ppt Q4 growth; domestic demand only 0.77ppt. This is entirely external-driven."
→ ING upgrading 2026 Taiwan GDP forecast to 6.8% from consensus 3.9% on continued tech strength
→ Reuters: "TSMC revenue Q3 2025 expected $33.1B, up 40.8% YY; 3nm + 5nm processes = 60% of total; TSMC output growth alone contributed nearly 4ppt to Taiwan GDP"
→ Natixis Economist Alicia Garcia Herrero: "Taiwan current account surplus >15% of GDP will draw heightened international scrutiny, fueling accusations of currency undervaluation"

COMMENT (HF sensitivity):
Dominant signal: Taiwan GDP 12.68% = HIGHEST QUARTERLY GROWTH SINCE Q3 1987 (38 years). This is NOT base effect (2024 was strong), it's a genuine AI/semiconductor boom. CRITICAL: 11.91ppt of 12.68ppt from NET EXPORTS (external) vs only 0.77ppt from domestic demand. This makes Taiwan extremely vulnerable to: (a) AI demand slowdown, (b) US tariffs on chips (currently exempt), (c) global tech cycle downturn.
Secondary: Full-year 2025 8.63% = highest since 2010, but unlike 2010 (post-GFC base effect), this is real momentum
Noise: Q4 beat of 4.18pp (12.68% vs 8.50% consensus) suggests economists STILL underestimating AI boom intensity; consensus 2026 forecast 3.9% likely too low (ING at 6.8% more realistic)
Reaction-function impact (CBC - Central Bank of China Taiwan): GDP 12.68% + CPI 1.7% (benign) = CBC in "no action needed" zone. Rate likely stays 2.00% through H1 2026. BUT: Pressure from US on currency appreciation rising (current account >15% GDP = "manipulation" risk). CBC may allow TWD to strengthen 3-5% in 2026 to appease US.
Transmission: TWD appreciation likely (both from fundamentals and US pressure). TWD strength = headwind to exporters but manageable given TSMC pricing power. Taiwan equity (TAIEX) supported by earnings (TSMC EPS growth 40%+), but vulnerable to: (a) AI bubble burst, (b) China-Taiwan tension spike, (c) US export controls on advanced chips.
Regime risk: Taiwan is in EXTREME concentration risk — TSMC alone = 4ppt of GDP growth, semiconductors = ~40% of exports. If AI demand plateaus or US restricts chip exports to China, Taiwan GDP could collapse from 12.68% to sub-2% in single quarter. This is "tech boom or bust" economy with no diversification.

FRIDAY 31 JAN — RELEASED

CHINA — NBS Manufacturing PMI (Jan)
• Actual: 49.3 vs Consensus: 50.0 vs Prior: 50.1

PROFESSIONAL COMMENTARY (aggregated from public sources):
→ NBS Chief Statistician Huo Lihui: "PMI fell as some industries entered traditional seasonal lull and effective market demand remained insufficient. Production sub-index 50.6 (still expansion), but new orders 49.2 (contraction)."
→ NBS data: High-tech manufacturing PMI 52.0 (bright spot, second month >52); Equipment manufacturing 50.1 (expansion); Consumer goods 48.3, high energy-consuming 47.9 (both contracting)
→ ING Economist: "January PMI 49.3 suggests December 50.1 uptick was likely a blip. Broad-based contraction raises doubts about imminent manufacturing recovery. Silver lining: ex-factory prices 50.6 (28-month high, first >50 in 20 months), raw material input prices 56.1 (20-month high) = deflation pressures may be easing."
→ Nomura Economist Jing Wang: "Growth momentum expected to remain weak in January, citing payback effects from consumer goods trade-in program last year and persistent property distress. These measures are far from enough to stabilize growth — Beijing will have to do much more in coming months to deliver annual GDP growth above 4.5% in 2026."
→ Caixin/RatingDog PMI (private survey, smaller export-oriented sample): 50.3 vs NBS 49.3 = divergence suggests PRIVATE/EXPORT firms doing better than STATE/DOMESTIC firms

COMMENT (HF sensitivity):
Dominant signal: China NBS PMI 49.3 = BACK TO CONTRACTION after single month of expansion (Dec 50.1). The divergence with Caixin PMI 50.3 is critical: STATE/DOMESTIC demand collapsing (NBS surveys large SOEs + domestic), PRIVATE/EXPORT holding (Caixin surveys SMEs + exporters). This confirms regime diagnosis: China's problem is DOMESTIC DEMAND COLLAPSE, not external weakness.
Secondary: Sub-indices paint clear picture — Production 50.6 (firms still producing), New Orders 49.2 (demand falling), New Export Orders 47.8 (export demand weakening too). This is classic "destocking" pattern: firms cutting production because inventories building.
Noise: January PMI often weak due to Lunar New Year seasonality (factories shut early, workers leave), so single month contraction not panic-worthy
Reaction-function impact (PBoC + Fiscal): NBS PMI 49.3 + Nomura assessment ("far from enough") = stimulus acceleration coming. Expect Q1 2026: (a) RRR cut 50bp, (b) MLF/LPR cut 10-15bp, (c) fiscal consumption vouchers expansion. March NPC (parliamentary session) likely announces fiscal deficit 4.0-4.5% of GDP (vs 3.8% prior).
Transmission: CNH weakening pressure (PMI contraction + policy easing = dovish CNY). PBoC likely allows CNY to drift to 7.40-7.50 vs USD (from current 7.30) to support exporters. China equity (CSI 300) vulnerable — PMI 49.3 = earnings downgrades coming, especially in consumer goods (PMI 48.3) and industrials. Only bright spot: high-tech (PMI 52.0) = continue to overweight AI/semiconductors (local champions like SMIC), underweight property/consumption.
Regime trigger: If Feb + March PMI also <50 (three consecutive months contraction) = PBOC forced into aggressive easing (100bp RRR cut + 25bp rate cut). Threshold: Q1 2026 IP growth <4.5% = panic mode.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CROSS-EM SYNTHESIS — WEEK 1
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

THEME: EXTREME DIVERGENCE — Growth/Inflation Scissors Opening

The Week 1 data reveals an unprecedented EM divergence, not just in growth rates but in the COMBINATION of growth and inflation outcomes:

**TIER 1 — PERFECT COMBO (Growth High + Inflation Low):**
• INDIA: IP 7.8% (26-month high) + PMI 56.8 Mfg / 59.3 Svc + CPI 1.33% YY (benign)
• TAIWAN: GDP 12.68% (38-year high) + CPI 1.7% YY (below target)

This is the "Goldilocks" scenario for EMs — strong growth without inflation pressure. Both benefit from EXTERNAL drivers (Taiwan = AI/chip exports; India = infrastructure spending + tech services exports) but India has stronger DOMESTIC resilience (consumer durables +12.3%, domestic new orders leading PMI).

**TIER 2 — STABLE (Growth Moderate + Inflation Anchored):**
• TURKEY: Reserves +6.36B (credibility rebuild) + inflation 47% YY but DECELERATING
• SOUTH AFRICA: Repo 6.75% hold, inflation mid-range, growth weak but stable

These are "muddling through" — no immediate crisis, but no breakout either.

**TIER 3 — STRESS (Growth Collapsing + Inflation/Policy Constraints):**
• CHINA: NBS PMI 49.3 (contraction) + domestic demand collapse + deflation risk (but easing)
• BRAZIL: Selic 15.00% (restrictive) + IP contracting + growth slowdown
• MEXICO: IGAE -0.1% (major miss) + core CPI sticky + Banxico easing limited

---

**CENTRAL BANK DIVERGENCE MAP:**

HIKING: None (RBA in DM is only hiker globally)
HOLDING (Hawkish Bias): Turkey CBT (50.00%, reserves improving but inflation 47%)
HOLDING (Neutral): India RBI (5.25%, no urgency either direction), Taiwan CBC (2.00%)
HOLDING (Dovish Bias): Brazil BCB (15.00%, first cut March/May), South Africa SARB (6.75%, gradual easing)
EASING PATH: Mexico Banxico (7.00% → 6.00% by end-2026), China PBoC (RRR/rate cuts coming Q1)

**CROSS-EM CENTRAL BANK URGENCY RANKING (Highest to Lowest):**
1. China PBoC (URGENT — PMI contraction, domestic demand collapse)
2. Brazil BCB (HIGH — growth slowing, inflation cooperating, easing imminent)
3. Mexico Banxico (MEDIUM — IGAE miss, core sticky, gradual easing)
4. South Africa SARB (LOW — patient, data-dependent, slow easing)
5. Turkey CBT (LOW — hawkish hold, reserves improving, credibility priority)
6. India RBI (ZERO — perfect hold setup, no action needed)
7. Taiwan CBC (ZERO — except for FX appreciation pressure from US)

---

**EM FX HIERARCHY (Week 1 Fundamentals):**

STRONGEST (Appreciation Pressure):
→ INR (growth 7.8% + inflation 1.33% + carry 4% real + current account improving)
→ TWD (GDP 12.68% + current account >15% GDP + US pressure to appreciate)

STABLE (Range-Bound):
→ ZAR (SARB patient, reserves stable, carry decent)
→ MXN (Banxico easing priced, IGAE weak but not crisis)

VULNERABLE (Depreciation Risk):
→ CNH (PMI 49.3 + easing coming + domestic demand collapse)
→ BRL (Selic 15% peak, cuts coming March, carry attractive but fading)
→ TRY (reserves improving BUT still fragile, inflation 47%, CA deficit)

**FX TRADES IMPLIED:**
Long INR vs CNH (growth differential + policy divergence)
Long TWD vs MXN (tech boom vs growth slowdown)
Avoid TRY (reserve improvement is tactical, structural problems remain)

---

**REGIME SHIFT SUMMARY:**

PRIOR REGIME (Early Jan 2026):
"China mixed signals; India strong; Taiwan tech boom intact; Turkey credibility rebuild; Brazil/Mexico gradual easing"

UPDATED REGIME (Post-Week 1):
**"EM DIVERGENCE EXTREME — India/Taiwan booming on domestic strength + tech exports (growth high + inflation low = perfect); China domestic demand collapsing (PMI 49.3, stimulus urgency rising); Brazil/Mexico growth softening (dovish pivots coming); Turkey reserves improving but fragile; South Africa patient."**

**DOMINANT CROSS-EM THEME:**
The GROWTH/INFLATION SCISSORS are opening — India/Taiwan have high growth + low inflation (central banks can hold forever), while China/Brazil/Mexico have low growth + policy constraints (China deflation, Brazil/Mexico inflation above target historically). This creates maximum EM FX dispersion and maximum alpha opportunity in EM equity selection (overweight India/Taiwan tech, underweight China consumer/property, neutral Brazil/Mexico).

**REGIME TRIGGERS (What Would Change This View):**

BULLISH TRIGGER (EM-wide rally):
→ China announces MASSIVE stimulus at March NPC (fiscal deficit >5% GDP + 100bp RRR cut + property support) = CNH stabilizes, EM risk-on
→ Fed cuts 50bp in March (dovish pivot) = EM FX rally across board
→ US-China trade deal (tariff rollback) = China export recovery, Taiwan/Korea benefit

BEARISH TRIGGER (EM-wide selloff):
→ Taiwan AI demand plateaus (Nvidia revenue miss, TSMC order cancellations) = Taiwan GDP collapses from 12.68% to <2%, TWD crashes
→ India inflation SPIKES (food shock, oil shock) = RBI forced to hike, INR weakens, equity selloff
→ China PMI <48 for 3 consecutive months (hard landing) = CNH 7.50+, EM contagion

NEUTRAL TRIGGER (Status Quo):
→ China gradual easing (25bp cuts, modest fiscal) without demand recovery = CNH drifts weaker, no EM contagion
→ India/Taiwan continue outperforming but at slower pace (India IP 6%, Taiwan GDP 8%) = still positive but less extreme
→ Brazil/Mexico easing cycles proceed as expected (gradual, data-dependent) = currencies range-bound

END WEEK 1 (JAN 23-30, 2026)

BOTTOM LINE — WEEK SYNTHESIS

What actually mattered:

China delivered a clean “mixed but managed” packet: GDP/IO beat while retail + investment disappointed. Net: production/exports holding up, domestic demand still fragile → reinforces targeted support rather than bazooka stimulus.

Turkey was the biggest regime-shaper: reserves surged and CBT cut less than feared (hawkish vs consensus). Net: credibility constraints eased, allowing controlled normalization.

Poland had a violent mix: industrial output upside shock + wage re-acceleration. Net: growth better, but wage pressure kills dovish optionality — easing expectations get capped.

Korea and Mexico both printed material growth downside (Korea GDP q/q negative; Mexico IGAE miss). Net: pockets of EM are flashing growth vulnerability even while tech proxies (Taiwan) look strong.

What did NOT:

South Africa CPI being exactly on consensus didn’t shift anything; the mining shock mattered more for growth risk, while retail upside just made the signal mixed.

Taiwan unemployment had no information content.

Reaction function shifts:

PBoC/China: no inflation constraint; domestic-demand weakness keeps pressure on fiscal/targeted credit, but headline growth beats reduce urgency.

CBT/Turkey: reserves rebuild shifts the regime toward “normalize cautiously,” less forced-hawk risk.

Banxico/Mexico: headline inflation helps, but growth miss increases easing pressure; core keeps the pace gradual.

BoK/Korea: downside GDP surprise increases dovish pressure, but constraints remain FX/financial stability.

BOTTOM LINE — WEEK SYNTHESIS

What actually mattered:

China (trade + credit): Big beats in exports/imports and stronger-than-expected TSF/loans were the week’s core EM impulse — “China not worsening” with a modest credit impulse, supporting CNH and EM beta through risk sentiment.

Brazil (activity cross-currents): Services output was a genuine downside signal, but retail + IBC-Br pushed back hard. Net: Brazil is stabilising with volatility, not a clean downshift — this caps aggressive dovish pricing unless inflation provides a stronger green light.

Turkey (external vs reserves tug-of-war): Current account deterioration was negative, but the reserve rebuild late-week is first-order positive. Net: TRY risk premium becomes more two-sided again — still credibility-driven, but less one-way stress.

What did NOT:

Rates decisions (BoK, NBP) were pure holds with no new impulse.

Most “final” CPI prints in CEE were confirmation, not catalysts.

Reaction-function shifts:

RBI: CPI downside surprise keeps policy optionality; WPI upside is a caution flag, not a trigger — net still “patient.”

BCB: Hard activity resilience (IBC-Br) pushes against an aggressive dovish narrative; easing expectations remain data-dependent on inflation and sustained softness.

China policy: Data supports the stance of targeted monetary support + fiscal execution rather than shock stimulus.

CBT: Reserves improved, which reduces forced-hawk risk, but external balance volatility keeps credibility as the binding constraint.

Brazil: The week was about growth downside becoming first-order (PMIs collapsing into <50 + industrial output y/y worsening). “Overall Comprehensive Risk” prints were non-catalysts across countries (no material signal unless they swing hard).

Taiwan CPI didn’t constrain anything; Taiwan trade momentum mattered more than price.

Reaction-function shifts (or not):

BCB: growth shock upgrades dovish asymmetry; inflation data did not fight it.

Banxico: disinflation continues, but core keeps the committee cautious → path remains gradual.

CBT: credibility/reserves dominate; easing talk remains constrained even with softer CPI.

China: policy retains room for support; no inflation penalty, but no clear demand re-acceleration either.
